Refutation of al-Sharif via al-Qarafi on Takleef Ma La Yutaq
Sanusi refutes al-Sharif's claim by citing al-Qarafi's report on the severity of obligation in usul al-din.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes al-Sharif's claim by presenting al-Qarafi's argument that obligation beyond capacity does occur in usul al-din.

Core Idea
Even exhaustive effort does not excuse ignorance in matters of creed.

Al-Sharif claimed that the obligation beyond capacity (takleef ma la yutaq) does not occur in the fundamentals of religion. Sanusi counters by citing al-Qarafi, who gives a stark example: a person who exhausts all effort to know a matter of usul al-din but remains ignorant is still considered a sinner and disbeliever. This shows that such obligation does occur.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recognize that al-Sharif argued that takleef ma la yutaq does not happen in usul al-din. Sanusi refutes this by quoting al-Qarafi.
This passage is a direct counter-argument.
2
Read al-Qarafi's report
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the extreme strictness described: even if one exhausts effort, if ignorance remains, he is sinful and a disbeliever.
Pay attention to the phrase 'آثم كافر'.
3
Analyze the example
Consider the example of the foolish woman in remote regions. Despite her inability to reason properly, she is still obligated with the details of usul al-din and punished for ignorance.
This illustrates the concept of obligation beyond capacity.
4
Reflect on implications
Think about why this passage is important in kalam. It shows that human capacity is not a condition for obligation in matters of belief.
Connects to broader discussions of divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الدين ، وما ادعاه الشريف مِنْ عدم وقوعِهِ فيها بمُجرَّدِ اجتهاده.. مُعارَضُ بنقل القرافي ضدَّ ذلك ، قال القرافي - على ما رأيتُ في نقل بعض المشايخ عنه - : ( وقد شدَّدَ صاحب الشرع في عقائدِ أصول الدين تشديداً عظيماً ؛ بحيثُ إِنَّ الإنسان لو بذل جهدَهُ واستفرغ وُسْعَهُ في رفع الجهلِ عنه في صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِ اللهِ تعالى أو في شيء مما يجبُ اعتقادُهُ مِنْ أصول الدين ، ولم يرتفع ذلك الجهلُ عنه . . فإنَّهُ آثم كافرُ على المشهورِ مِنَ المذاهب ، معَ أَنَّهُ قد أوصل الاجتهاد حدَّهُ ، وصارَ الجهل له ضرورياً لا يمكنه دفعُهُ ، ومع ذلك لم يُعذَر ، حتى صارَتْ هذه الصورة ممَّا يُعتقَدُ أَنَّهَا مِنْ وقوع تكليف ما لا يُطاق ؛ فإنَّ تكليف المرأةِ البلهاء الفاسدة المزاج في الأقاليم المنحرفة عمَّا يُوجِبُ استقامة العقل ؛ كأقاصي بلادِ السُّودان وأقاصي بلادِ التركِ .. ممَّا لا يُطاقُ ؛ فإنَّ هذهِ الأقاليم لا يكونُ للعقل فيها كبير رونق ، ولذلك قال تعالى في بلادِ التركِ وَجَدَ مِن دُونِهِمَا قَوْمًا لَّا يَكَادُونَ يَفْقَهُونَ قَوْلًا ﴾ [الكهف : ۹۳] ، ومع ذلك فهم مُكلَّفونَ بدقائقِ أصولِ الدين ودلائل التوحيد ، ومُخلَّدونَ بالجهلِ في النارِ) وإنما ساق كلامه هنا ليبينَ وقوع التكليف بما لا يُطاق في أصول الدين على قول
The fundamentals of religion, and what al-Sharif claimed of its not occurring by mere ijtihad... is countered by the transmission from al-Qarafi contrary to that. Al-Qarafi said – according to what I have seen in the transmission of some shaykhs about him –: 'The Lawgiver has placed extreme strictness in the beliefs of the fundamentals of religion, to the extent that if a person exerts his effort and exhausts his capacity in removing ignorance from himself regarding an attribute of Allah the Exalted or something that must be believed from the fundamentals of religion, and that ignorance does not leave him... then he is a sinner, a disbeliever according to the well-known of the schools, despite the fact that he has brought ijtihad to its limit and ignorance became necessary for him, not being able to repel it. Yet he was not excused, until this case came to be considered as an occurrence of obligation beyond capacity. For the obligation upon a foolish woman of corrupt temperament in regions deviating from what necessitates soundness of intellect – like the extremes of the lands of the Sudan and the extremes of the lands of the Turks – is unbearable. For these regions do not have much luster of intellect. Therefore Allah the Exalted said concerning the land of the Turks: 'He found beyond them a people who could scarcely understand a word' [al-Kahf: 93]. Yet they are charged with the minutiae of the fundamentals of religion and the proofs of tawhid, and are eternally in the Fire due to ignorance.' And he only brought his speech here to show the occurrence of the obligation beyond capacity in the fundamentals of religion according to a view.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Sharif's claim that the obligation beyond capacity (takleef ma la yutaq) does not occur in the fundamentals of religion (usul al-din). The author counters this by quoting al-Qarafi's report. Al-Qarafi describes the extreme strictness of the Lawgiver in matters of 'aqidah: even if a person exhausts all effort to remove ignorance about an attribute of Allah or a necessary belief, and that ignorance persists, he is deemed sinful and a disbeliever according to the majority of schools. This is despite the fact that the person has reached the limit of ijtihad and the ignorance became unavoidable. This case is considered an instance of imposing an obligation beyond capacity. Al-Qarafi gives the example of a foolish woman in regions with weak intellects (like remote areas of Sudan and Turkey) who cannot achieve sound reasoning. Allah mentions such people in the Qur'an (al-Kahf: 93). Yet they are still obligated with the details of usul al-din and the proofs of tawhid, and they are punished eternally in the Fire for their ignorance. The author then remarks that al-Qarafi brought this example to demonstrate that the obligation beyond capacity does occur in usul al-din, according to one view.

التكليف بما لا يطاق
الاجتهاد
الجهل

Misconception: If someone exhausts all effort to learn a matter of usul al-din and still remains ignorant, they are excused.
Correction: According to al-Qarafi, such a person is still sinful and a disbeliever, showing that ignorance is not excused.

D) He is excused if the ignorance is unavoidable.

Key Takeaway
Takleef ma la yutaq (obligation beyond capacity) does occur in usul al-din, as shown by al-Qarafi's example of the foolish woman who is held accountable despite her inability to understand.

Faith Requires Certainty and Knowledge through Correct Reasoning
Sanusi states the requirement of certainty and knowledge for faith, citing hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true faith (īmān) requires certainty (yaqīn) and knowledge (ma‘rifa), which can only be achieved through correct reasoning (al-naẓar al-ṣaḥīḥ), as supported by authentic hadith.

Core Idea
Faith needs more than words—it needs certainty and knowledge from reasoning.

This lesson explores the foundational requirement of faith according to Sanusi: it must be based on certainty and knowledge, not mere utterance. He cites two key hadiths that emphasize inner certainty and knowledge. Let’s see what the source says.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from Sanusi
Read the Arabic passage once to get the gist. Then read the translation. Notice the claim and the two hadiths.
2
Identify the two hadiths
Find the hadith from Abu Huraira and the one from Muslim. Observe what each requires: certainty (yaqīn) in the heart and knowledge of the shahada.
Both hadiths link salvation to inner conviction.
3
Reflect on correct reasoning
Consider why Sanusi says these qualities are only attained through correct reasoning (al-naẓar al-ṣaḥīḥ). Think about the role of intellectual effort in faith.
This sets the stage for the next lesson on imitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى (۱)؛ لأنَّ المطلوب في الإيمانِ اليقين والمعرفة ، وذلك لا يكونُ إلا بالنظر الصحيح. وفي حديث أبي هريرةَ رضي الله تعالى عنه : ( مَنْ لَقِيتَ وَرَاءَ هَذَا الْحَائِطِ يَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إلا اللهُ مُسْتَيْقِناً قَلْبُهُ . . فَبَشِّرْهُ بِالْجَنَّةِ (٢) . وفي ( مسلم ) : ( مَنْ مَاتَ وَهُوَ يَعْلَمُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إلا الله . . دَخَلَ الْجَنَّةَ ((۳) . فانظر كيف شرط في هذين الحديثين اليقين والعلم ، وهما ضدَّانِ ولا يصح أنْ يُقالَ : ( الجزم لأجل التقليد علم ) لأنَّهُ لو كانَ ذلكَ الجزمُ علماً .. لزم اجتماع الضدين (٥) ; في الجزم بحدوثه تقليداً ، والجزم بقدمِهِ كذلكَ أيضاً ; لأنَّ العلم صفةٌ لا تحتمل النقيض بوجه ، فيلزمُ أنْ يكونَ العالم في نفس الأمر قديماً وحادثاً ! وذلكَ ممَّا لا يُعقَلُ . وهذان الحديثانِ يُفسّرانَ كلَّ ما أُجمِلَ مِنْ أحاديث الشهادتين ، وأنَّها محمولةٌ على العلم واليقين ، لا على مُجرَّدِ النطق والاكتفاء فيهما بالتقليد .
He (God) is exalted (1); because what is required in faith is certainty (al-yaqīn) and knowledge (al-ma‘rifa), and that is only attained through correct reasoning (al-naẓar al-ṣaḥīḥ). And in the hadith of Abu Hurairah, may God be pleased with him: 'Whomever you meet behind this wall bearing witness that there is no god but God, with his heart certain... then give him glad tidings of Paradise' (2). And in Muslim: 'Whoever dies while he knows that there is no god but God... enters Paradise' (3). So see how He required in these two hadiths certainty and knowledge, and they are opposites, and it is not correct to say: 'The judgment (al-jazzm) for the sake of imitation (al-taqlīd) is knowledge' because if that judgment were knowledge... then the union of opposites would necessarily result (4): in judging its contingency (al-ḥudūth) by imitation, and judging its eternity (al-qidam) likewise also; because knowledge is an attribute that does not admit of the opposite in any way, so it would necessarily follow that the knower (al-‘ālim) is in reality both eternal and contingent! And that is inconceivable. And these two hadiths explain all that is summarized from the hadiths of the two testimonies, and that they are carried upon knowledge and certainty, not upon mere utterance and being content in them with imitation.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a proof that true faith (īmān) requires certainty (yaqīn) and knowledge (ma‘rifa), which can only be obtained through correct reasoning (naẓar ṣaḥīḥ). Sanusi begins by stating the goal of faith: certainty and knowledge, and that this is not possible except through correct reasoning. He then cites two hadiths: one from Abu Huraira where the Prophet says to give glad tidings of Paradise to anyone who meets him behind the wall with a heart certain of the shahada, and another from Muslim that whoever dies knowing that there is no god but God enters Paradise. These hadiths show that certainty and knowledge are required. Then he addresses a potential objection: can one achieve knowledge through imitation (taqlīd)? He argues that if mere judgment (jazzm) based on imitation were considered knowledge, then a person could simultaneously have contradictory judgments (e.g., that the world is both contingent and eternal), which is impossible because knowledge is an attribute that cannot admit its opposite. Thus imitation cannot produce genuine knowledge. He concludes that these two hadiths explain that the shahada hadiths are to be understood as requiring knowledge and certainty, not just utterance and contentment with imitation.

Key Terms
اليقين
المعرفة
النظر الصحيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Certainty and imitation

D) Utterance and imitation

Key Takeaway
Faith requires certainty and knowledge, which are only attained through correct reasoning.

Why Imitation Cannot Produce True Knowledge
Sanusi argues that imitation cannot yield knowledge, using the union of opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why imitation (taqlīd) cannot produce genuine knowledge in matters of faith, using Sanusi's argument about the impossibility of contradictory judgments.

Core Idea
If imitation produced knowledge, you could believe contradictions—impossible.

Sanusi now addresses a potential objection: Could imitation yield knowledge? He argues that if imitation were valid, a person could hold contradictory beliefs simultaneously, which is impossible for true knowledge. Let’s unpack this logical argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from Sanusi
Read from 'fānẓur kayfa sharṭa' to the end. Note the logical structure: a claim, a hypothetical, and a conclusion.
2
Identify the hypothetical scenario
Sanusi imagines someone judging the world as contingent by imitation and also judging it as eternal by imitation. Understand what this means.
These are opposite judgments.
3
Understand why knowledge cannot admit opposites
Knowledge is an attribute that cannot hold true for opposite things simultaneously. If imitation produced knowledge, one could 'know' both contingency and eternity—a contradiction.
This shows the absurdity.
4
Conclude the lesson
Therefore, imitation does not produce knowledge. The hadiths require real certainty and knowledge, not imitation.

Refuting the Jibril Hadith Objection for Imitation
Sanusi refutes the objection that the Jibril hadith permits imitation in matters of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Jibril hadith does not sanction imitation in faith and why knowledge (ma'rifa) requires reasoning (nazar).

Core Idea
The Jibril hadith presupposes knowledge, and knowledge demands reasoning – imitation is insufficient.

This lesson examines an objection raised by those who claim that the famous hadith of Jibril proves that imitation is acceptable in matters of faith. Sanusi shows that this inference is false because the hadith's definition of faith implies knowledge, which can only be attained through reasoning, not blind imitation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection from the Jibril hadith
Read the passage and identify the argument that some people make: the Prophet enumerated the articles of faith without mentioning proofs, so imitation suffices.
The objection is based on an omission of reasoning in the hadith.
2
Identify Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi declares the inference 'definitively false' (bāṭil qaṭ‘an). Find the reason he gives.
3
Learn the two interpretations of the hadith
The Prophet's words are interpreted by al-Ash‘ari as 'to know' and by al-Qāḍī as 'to speak to oneself following knowledge.' Both require knowledge.
Knowledge (ma‘rifa) is either the essence of faith or necessary for it.
4
Connect knowledge to reasoning
Sanusi concludes that knowledge is only attained through reasoning (naẓar), so the hadith does not dispense with reasoning.
Thus, imitation is insufficient for true faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وممَّا يَركنُ إليه في الاكتفاء بالتقليدِ بعضُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : الحديث الصحيحُ المشهورُ ; وهو حديث عبدِ اللهِ بنِ عمرَ عن رضي الله عنهما في سؤالِ جبريل عليه السلام النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلّمَ عنِ الإيمان والإسلام والإحسان (۱) ، في تفسيرِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لها بما هو معروف مشهورٌ ، فيقولُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : دلَّ الحديث على أنَّ مَنْ حفظَ تلك الخصال المفسَّرَ بها الإيمان وفهمها واعتقدها ولو بالتقليد .. فهو مؤمن ; إذ لو كانَ حصولها بالنظر شرطاً في كونها إيماناً لَمَا اقتصر النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في تفسيرِ الإِيمَانِ على عدها دونَ ذكرِ أدلَّتِها . وهذا الأخذُ مِنَ الحديثِ باطل قطعاً ; لأنَّ قولَه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في شرح الإيمانِ : « أَنْ تُؤْمِنَ بِاللهِ . . . (۲) إلى آخرِهِ : معناه عند الشيخ الأشعري : أن تعرف ذلك ، وعند القاضي وغيرِهِ تُحدِّثَ نفْسَكَ بذلك حديثاً تابعاً للمعرفة(۳) ، وعلى كلا القولين فالمعرفة التي هي نفس الإيمان أو لازمةٌ له.. لا تحصل إلا بالنظر .
And among that which some of those who have no insight rely upon for being content with imitation (al-taqlīd): the famous authentic hadith; and it is the hadith of ‘Abd Allāh ibn ‘Umar, on the authority of his father, may God be pleased with them both, concerning Gabriel's questioning of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, about faith (īmān), Islam (islām), and excellence (iḥsān) (1), in his explanation, peace and blessings be upon him, of them with what is well-known and famous. So one who has no insight says: The hadith indicates that whoever memorizes those characteristics by which faith is explained, understands them, and believes them, even if by imitation... then he is a believer; because if attaining them by reasoning (al-naẓar) were a condition for them being faith, the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, would not have limited himself in explaining faith to enumerating them without mentioning their proofs. And this inference from the hadith is definitively false; because his statement, peace and blessings be upon him, in explaining faith: 'That you believe in God... (2) to its end' – its meaning according to Shaykh al-Ash‘arī is: that you know that, and according to al-Qāḍī and others: that you speak to yourself with that speech following knowledge (3). And on both statements, knowledge (al-ma‘rifa) which is either the essence of faith or necessary for it.. is not attained except through reasoning.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised by those who argue that imitation (taqlīd) is sufficient for faith based on the famous hadith of Jibril (Gabriel). Sanusi identifies the objection: the hadith of Jibril, in which the Prophet defines faith as believing in God, His angels, etc., does not mention the need for reasoning. Therefore, some argue that merely memorizing and believing these items, even by imitation, makes one a believer. Sanusi responds decisively (bāṭil qaṭ‘an) that this inference is invalid. First, he clarifies the meaning of the Prophet's statement 'that you believe in God...' According to Imam al-Ash‘arī, this means 'that you know that' (an ta‘rifa dhālika). According to al-Qāḍī and others, it means to speak to oneself with a speech that follows knowledge. In both interpretations, knowledge (ma‘rifa) is either the essence of faith or a necessary concomitant of it. And knowledge can only be attained through reasoning (naẓar). Thus the Jibril hadith does not dispense with reasoning; rather, it presupposes knowledge obtained through reasoning. Therefore, imitation is insufficient.

Key Terms
التقليد
الإيمان
المعرفة
النظر
الشيخ الأشعري
القاضي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Jibril hadith removes the need for reasoning in faith because the Prophet did not mention proofs.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the hadith's definition of faith implies knowledge, and knowledge requires reasoning; thus imitation is insufficient.

Checkpoint
How does Sanusi refute the claim that the Jibril hadith permits imitation in faith?
A) By saying the hadith is weak.
B) By explaining that the hadith's definition of faith implies knowledge, which can only be attained through reasoning.
C) By saying the hadith was abrogated.
D) By arguing that the hadith doesn't apply to all people.

Key Takeaway
The Jibril hadith does not permit imitation; it presupposes knowledge, which must be attained through reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever simply accepted the creed you were taught as a child without personally reasoning to its truth? If so, is your faith based on imitation (taqlīd) or certitude? What will you do today to strengthen it through reflection?
?
If true faith requires knowledge (ma'rifa) attained by reasoning, do you truly know God and His attributes, or are you just repeating words? Commit to studying one proof for God's existence this week.
?
The hadith of Jibril does not excuse you from thinking. Are you willing to question and examine your beliefs as Sanusi demands, even if it is uncomfortable? What is holding you back?

The Five Opinions on Divine Guidance
Enumeration of five opinions on the meaning of divine guidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five scholarly opinions on the meaning of divine guidance (huda) as recorded by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Guidance means different things to different scholars.

Sanusi opens this section by reporting a key theological disagreement: what exactly is the guidance (huda) that Allah bestows? The answer is not obvious, and five distinct positions were held. This lesson introduces those five opinions, setting the stage for the author's preferred interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration
Read the Arabic sentence listing the five opinions. Notice the concise style.
2
Identify each opinion
Match each Arabic term with its translation. Understand what each represents.
3
Consider the significance
Why list five opinions? This shows the depth of theological discussion on a seemingly simple term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف الناسُ في هدى الله تعالى الذي يهدي بِهِ مَنْ يَشَاءُ مِنْ عبادِهِ ، فقيل : هو الإيمانُ ، وقيل : هو العلم ، وقيل : هو الدليلُ ، وقيل : هو الكتاب ، وقيل : هو البيانُ فأَمَّا مَنْ قالَ : هو الإيمانُ . . فقد نظر إلى قوله سبحانه وتعالى : اللهُ نُورُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ﴾ [النور : ٣٥] ، قالَ ابنُ عباس : هادي أهلِ السماوات والأرض هي قالوا : وإِنَّما كَنَّى بالمشكاة .. عن صدرِ المؤمن ؛ فإنَّ المشكاة الكَوَّةُ غيرُ النافذة ، وكنَّى بالمصباح عن الإيمان الثابت في قلبه ، وكنى بالزجاجةِ عن القلبِ ، والشجرةُ المباركة دعوة الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ وسَنتُهمُ القويم ، وذكر الزيتونة لصفاء دُهنِها ، وأَنَّ الفساد لا يدخلُهُ ، فلا يتعفَّنُ ولا يخامرُ العقل ويفسده ، وهو يعلو على كل ما يُجعَلُ معَهُ مِنَ المائعاتِ ، فكذلك الإيمانُ لا يتضعضعُ أركانه ، ولا يضعفُ سلطانه ، ولا يتحيَّرُ برهانه ، ولا يُخافُ معَ الغفلة نقصانه ، وهو الظاهرُ على كل دين ؛ لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ وَلَوْ كَرِهَ الْمُشْرِكُونَ ﴾ [التوبة : ٣٣) .
Then the people differed concerning the guidance of Allah by which He guides whom He wills of His servants. It was said: it is faith, and it was said: it is knowledge, and it was said: it is the proof, and it was said: it is the Book, and it was said: it is the explanation. As for those who said it is faith, they looked to His saying, Exalted: 'Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth' [24:35]. Ibn Abbas said: 'The Guide of the inhabitants of the heavens and the earth.' They said: He only used the niche as a metaphor for the chest of the believer, for the niche is a non-penetrating hole. He used the lamp as a metaphor for the faith firmly fixed in his heart, and He used the glass as a metaphor for the heart. The blessed tree [represents] the call of the prophets, peace be upon them, and their straight path. He mentioned the olive for the purity of its oil and that corruption does not enter it, so it does not become putrid nor does it confuse the intellect and spoil it, and it rises above all liquids mixed with it. Similarly, faith: its pillars do not weaken, its authority does not become feeble, its proof does not become confused, and its deficiency is not feared with heedlessness. It is manifest over every religion, so that He may cause it to prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it [9:33].
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive treatment of the meaning of divine guidance (huda). It first lists five scholarly opinions: guidance is faith (iman), knowledge (ilm), proof (dalil), the Book (kitab), or explanation (bayan). The author then focuses on the view that guidance is faith, drawing evidence from the Light Verse (Ayat al-Nur, 24:35). The interpretation follows: the niche (mishkah) is the chest of the believer, the lamp (misbah) is faith, the glass (zujajah) is the heart. The blessed olive tree represents the call of the prophets. The olive oil's qualities—purity, resistance to corruption, and ability to float—are analogized to faith's qualities: strong pillars, unshaken authority, clear proof, immunity to loss during heedlessness, and supremacy over all religions. The passage concludes with a quote from Surah al-Tawbah (9:33) proclaiming the final victory of true religion.

Key Terms
هدى
إيمان
علم
دليل
كتاب
بيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume guidance has only one meaning; the passage shows multiple valid interpretations.
Correction: Scholars differed on the precise meaning of huda, each supported by scriptural evidence.

Checkpoint
How many opinions on the meaning of guidance are listed in the passage?
A) 3
B) 4
C) 5
D) 6

Key Takeaway
Sanusi records five distinct scholarly opinions on what divine guidance (huda) is, showing its rich theological meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the five aspects of guidance—faith, knowledge, proof, the Book, or explanation—do you rely on most in your daily life? Which one do you neglect? Commit today to strengthening one neglected aspect.
?
The scholars differed on the meaning of guidance, showing its depth. Is your own understanding of guidance limited to just 'being guided' without inner transformation? What would change if you saw guidance as also requiring active knowledge and proof?
?
Guidance includes both internal (faith, knowledge) and external (proof, Book, explanation) elements. Are you seeking both, or only relying on external rituals without internal conviction? What step will you take this week to deepen your inner connection to divine guidance?

The Light Verse Interpretation: Guidance as Faith
Detailed metaphorical interpretation of the Light Verse supporting guidance as faith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Light Verse (24:35) is interpreted to support the view that divine guidance is faith, through a detailed metaphor.

Core Idea
Faith is like a pure oil that never corrupts.

After listing the five opinions, Sanusi focuses on the view that guidance is faith, supporting it with a profound metaphorical interpretation of the Light Verse. Each element of the verse symbolizes a part of the believer's inner state, and the qualities of olive oil are analogized to the strength and purity of faith. This lesson unpacks that rich symbolism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the symbolic language.
2
Identify each symbol
Make a list: niche, lamp, glass, tree, oil. Write what each represents according to the scholars.
3
Understand the analogy
How does the oil's purity relate to faith? The passage explains that faith does not weaken.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with a verse about prevailing religion. How does this support faith as guidance?

It is manifest over every religion, so that He may cause it to prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it [9:33].

Faith Requires Knowledge Based on Decisive Proof
The author refutes equating faith and guidance, and defines true guidance as knowledge through decisive proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why true faith requires knowledge (ʿilm) based on a decisive proof, and why mere imitation (taqlīd) or conjecture (ẓann) does not constitute genuine guidance.

Core Idea
True guidance is knowledge with meta-awareness of how it is known.

The author challenges the idea that faith is simply guidance. He argues that faith needs a foundational light—knowledge—which itself must be established through decisive proof. This lesson unpacks his argument and the crucial distinction between genuine knowledge and mere conjecture.

Guided Path
1
Understand the refutation
Read the opening lines where the author dismisses the claim that faith is identical to guidance. Note that he says faith is a *type* of guidance, not guidance itself.
This sets up the need for a deeper component.
2
Grasp the necessity of decisive proof
Follow the argument: faith needs another light, which is knowledge. This knowledge must come from a decisive proof, and the scholar reflects until the intellect testifies to the proof’s validity, resulting in knowing *how* he knows.
Pay attention to the phrase 'knows how he knows' – it is key.
3
Study the dictum and Quranic support
Read the dictum of ahl al-taḥqīq: one who knows without knowing how does not truly know. Then see how two Quranic verses reinforce that guidance is knowledge and that blind imitation leads to misguidance.
The verses contrast those whose hearts are sealed with those who are guided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذهِ الطائفةُ التي ذهبَتْ إلى أنَّ الإيمان هو الهدى ليسَ ما صارَتْ إليه كذلك ، بل هو مِنْ ضروبِ الهدى ؛ فإِنَّ الإيمانَ يُحتاجُ في ثبوتِهِ إلى نورٍ آخر هو هدىً في نفسِهِ ؛ وهو العلم بما يُؤْمِنُ بهِ ، وهذا العلم لا بد وأن يكونَ ثابتاً عن دليل قاطع وقد وفَّقَ اللهُ العالِمَ للنظرِ والفكرِ في تلك الأدلَّةِ ، حتى تشهد لهُ ضرورة العقلِ بكيفيَّةِ أداء الدليل إلى العلم ، فعند ذلكَ يَعلَمُ ، ويَعلَمُ كيف عَلِمَ ، ولذا قالَ  َأهلُ التحقيقِ : مَنْ عَلِمَ ولم يعلم كيفَ عَلِمَ .. فلم يعلم ؛ إنما توهم نفسَهُ عالمةً ، ورتبتها الظن ، ودليلها التقليد ، أَوَلَوْ كَانَ ءَابَآؤُهُمْ لَا يَعْقِلُونَ شَيْئًا وَلَا يَهْتَدُونَ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٧٠] ، أَوَلَوْ كَانَ الشَّيْطَانُ يَدْعُوهُمْ إِلَى عَذَابِ السَّعِيرِ ﴾ [القمان : ۲۱] ؟! وهذا يُؤيد قولَ مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّ الهدى هو العلمُ ؛ فإِنَّ مَنْ فهم عن الله تعالى فقد اهتدى ، ومَنْ لم يفهم عنِ اللهِ تعالى آياتِهِ فقد ضلَّ وغوى ، وَمِنهُم مَّن يَسْتَمِعُ إِلَيْكَ حَتَّى إِذَا خَرَجُوا مِنْ عِندِكَ قَالُوا لِلَّذِينَ أُوتُوا العلم مَاذَا قَالَ عَائِفاً أُوْلَيكَ الَّذِينَ طَبَعَ اللَّهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ وَاتَّبعوا أَهْوَاءَ هُمْ * وَالَّذِينَ اهْتَدَوْا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى وَانَهُمْ تَقُونَهُمْ ﴾ [محمد : ١٦-١٧] .
And this group that went to the view that faith is guidance—what they have arrived at is not as such; rather it is one of the types of guidance. For faith, in its establishment, needs another light that is itself guidance; and it is knowledge of what one believes. And this knowledge must necessarily be established by a decisive proof. And Allah has granted success to the scholar for contemplation and reflection upon those proofs until the necessity of the intellect testifies to him concerning the manner in which the proof leads to knowledge. So at that point he knows, and he knows how he knows. Hence the people of verification said: 'Whoever knows and does not know how he knows, then he does not know; he only imagines himself to be knowledgeable, and his rank is conjecture, and his proof is imitation.' 'Even if their fathers did not understand anything and were not guided?' [Surah al-Baqarah 170], 'Even if Satan calls them to the punishment of the Blaze?' [Surah Luqman 21]. And this supports the saying of those who said: Guidance is knowledge. For whoever understands from Allah Almighty has been guided, and whoever does not understand Allah's signs has strayed and gone astray. 'And among them are those who listen to you until when they leave from your presence, they say to those who have been given knowledge: "What did he say just now?" Those are the ones upon whose hearts Allah has sealed and they have followed their own desires. And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance and gives them their piety.' [Surah Muhammad 16-17].
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a particular claim that faith (īmān) is identical to guidance (hudā). The author argues that those who hold this view have missed the mark; faith is rather one species of guidance. Faith requires a secondary light (nūr) that is itself guidance, and that light is knowledge (ʿilm) of the object of faith. This knowledge must be based on a decisive proof (dalīl qāṭiʿ). The scholar is enabled by Allah to contemplate and reflect on proofs until the necessity of the intellect (ḍarūrat al-ʿaql) testifies to how the proof leads to knowledge. At that point, the knower knows and knows how he knows. The author then cites the dictum of the people of verification (ahl al-taḥqīq): one who knows without knowing how he knows does not truly know; his knowledge is mere imagination, his rank is conjecture (ẓann), and his evidence is imitation (taqlīd). This is reinforced by two Quranic verses that question blind following of ancestors and of Satan. The author concludes by affirming that guidance is knowledge: understanding from Allah is guidance, and failure to understand His signs is misguidance. The final verses from Sūrat Muḥammad distinguish between those who hear but do not comprehend (their hearts sealed) and those who are guided and increase in guidance.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الهدى
العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can have true faith (īmān) simply by blindly following others (taqlīd) without understanding the proofs.
Correction: The passage argues that faith requires knowledge based on a decisive proof, and that knowledge must include awareness of how the proof leads to certainty. Without this, one's belief is only conjecture (ẓann) and imitation (taqlīd), not genuine faith.

Checkpoint
According to the people of verification, what is the status of someone who knows but does not know how he knows?
A) He is a true scholar
B) He knows but his knowledge is incomplete
C) He does not truly know; his rank is conjecture
D) He is excused because he is a muqallid

Key Takeaway
True guidance is knowledge attained through decisive proof, accompanied by awareness of how that knowledge is derived, as opposed to mere imitation or conjecture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you know how you know what you believe? Can you trace each of your core Islamic beliefs back to a decisive proof that you have personally reflected upon until your intellect testified to its truth? If not, are you content with conjecture and imitation?
?
When you read the Quran, do you understand directly from Allah, or do you rely on what others say? The passage says that whoever does not understand Allah’s signs has strayed. Have you ever asked yourself what it means to truly 'understand' an ayah, not just memorize its translation?
?
The scholars said: 'Whoever knows and does not know how he knows, does not know.' If someone were to ask you right now how you know that Allah exists, could you explain the proof and the process by which your intellect became certain? If not, is your faith truly yours, or inherited?

Faith Requires Knowledge from Decisive Proof
Sanusi argues that faith requires decisive proof and reflective knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true faith, according to Sanusi, requires a decisive proof and self-reflective knowledge, not mere imitation or conjecture.

Core Idea
True faith is impossible without decisive proof and knowing how you know.

Sanusi refutes the notion that faith is simply a feeling or blind acceptance. He insists that faith must be grounded in certain knowledge derived from a decisive proof. This passage distinguishes between genuine knowledge and mere conjecture, using reason and Quranic verses to establish the necessity of reflection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim about faith and guidance
Sanusi begins by addressing a group that equates faith with guidance. Read the opening lines to grasp his nuance: faith is a type of guidance, but it requires another light.
2
Identify the role of decisive proof
Sanusi states that faith needs a decisive proof (dali qati). Notice how he links knowledge to this proof and emphasizes the process of reflection (nazar) and thinking (fikr).
3
Contrast with imitation and conjecture
The passage then contrasts the true knower with one who only imagines knowing. Find the quote from the people of verification and the Quranic verses. What is the rank of the imitator?
4
Reflect on the meaning of 'knowing how you know'
Sanusi says that true knowledge includes knowing how you know. Consider why this is important for faith to be valid.
This self-awareness is a key marker of certain knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذهِ الطائفةُ التي ذهبَتْ إلى أنَّ الإيمان هو الهدى ليسَ ما صارَتْ إليه كذلك ، بل هو مِنْ ضروبِ الهدى ; فإِنَّ الإيمانَ يُحتاجُ في ثبوتِهِ إلى نورٍ آخر هو هدىً في نفسِهِ ; وهو العلم بما يُؤْمِنُ بهِ ، وهذا العلم لا بد وأن يكونَ ثابتاً عن دليل قاطع وقد وفَّقَ اللهُ العالِمَ للنظرِ والفكرِ في تلك الأدلَّةِ ، حتى تشهد لهُ ضرورة العقلِ بكيفيَّةِ أداء الدليل إلى العلم ، فعند ذلكَ يَعلَمُ ، ويَعلَمُ كيف عَلِمَ ، ولذا قالَ أهلُ التحقيقِ : مَنْ عَلِمَ ولم يعلم كيفَ عَلِمَ .. فلم يعلم ; إنما توهم نفسَهُ عالمةً ، ورتبتها الظن ، ودليلها التقليد ، أَوَلَوْ كَانَ ءَابَآؤُهُمْ لَا يَعْقِلُونَ شَيْئًا وَلَا يَهْتَدُونَ ) [البقرة : ١٧٠] ، أَوَلَوْ كَانَ الشَّيْطَانُ يَدْعُوهُمْ إِلَى عَذَابِ السَّعِيرِ ) [لقمان : ٢١] ؟!
And this group that held that faith is guidance is not as they became, rather it is a type of guidance; for faith needs in its establishment another light which is guidance in itself; and it is knowledge of what one believes in, and this knowledge must be established by a decisive proof. And Allah has guided the scholar to reflection and thinking in those proofs, until the necessity of the intellect testifies to him about the manner of the proof's leading to knowledge, so then he knows, and he knows how he knows. Therefore the people of verification said: 'Whoever knows but does not know how he knows ... does not know; he only imagines himself knowing, and his rank is conjecture, and his proof is imitation.' 'Even if their fathers understood nothing and were not guided' [Al-Baqara 2:170], 'Even if Satan calls them to the punishment of the Blaze' [Luqman 31:21]?!
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the nature of true faith and knowledge. Sanusi begins by stating that the group which said faith is guidance did not mean that faith itself is guidance in the sense they imagined, but rather that it is a type of guidance. He explains that faith requires another light to be established, which is guidance in itself: that light is knowledge of what one believes in. This knowledge must be based on a decisive proof (dali qati). Sanusi then describes the process: Allah guides the scholar to reflection (nazar) and thinking (fikr) on those proofs until the necessity of the intellect testifies how the proof leads to knowledge. Consequently, he knows and knows how he knows. This is contrasted with the one who knows but does not know how he knows; such a person does not truly know—he only imagines himself knowing. His rank is conjecture (zann) and his evidence is imitation (taqlid). Sanusi then supports this with two Quranic verses that condemn blind following of ancestors without understanding.

Correction: Sanusi emphasizes faith requires decisive proof and reflective knowledge of how one knows.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the condition for true knowledge of faith?
A) Simple acceptance without investigation
B) Knowledge based on a decisive proof and knowing how one knows
C) Merely believing in one's heart
D) Following the scholars blindly

Key Takeaway
Faith must be built on decisive proof and self-aware knowledge, not on imitation or conjecture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you know how you know that God exists, or are you merely following what you were taught? Today, commit to finding at least one decisive proof and understanding it rationally so that you truly know.
?
When you reflect on your belief in Islam, can you honestly say you know the proofs behind it? If not, what step will you take to move from imitation to certainty, knowing that faith requires you to know how you know?
?
The passage says if you know but do not know how you know, you do not really know—you only imagine it. How does that challenge the level of your own faith? Will you seek the depth of reflective knowledge, or remain comfortable with conjecture?

Guidance is Knowledge
Sanusi asserts guidance as knowledge with Quran and Ghazali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's argument that true guidance is inseparable from knowledge, supported by Quranic verses and a Ghazali illustration.

Core Idea
Guidance is not mere feeling; it is knowledge of Allah.

Sanusi begins by endorsing the position that guidance (huda) is essentially knowledge ('ilm). He references a Quranic verse contrasting those who listen but do not understand with those who are guided and increased in guidance. To clarify the nature of true understanding, he quotes al-Ghazali's example of how the dullard and the insightful person perceive the universal glorification of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the flow.
Notice the Quranic verses and the Ghazali quote.
2
Identify the definition of guidance
Find where Sanusi states that guidance is knowledge. Note the explanation: whoever understands from Allah is guided.
This is the central claim.
3
Understand the Quranic evidence
Look at verses 47:16-17: the first describes those who don't understand, the second says the guided are increased in guidance and given piety.
These verses directly support the link between guidance and knowledge.
4
Reflect on the Ghazali illustration
Consider the example of the dullard vs. the insightful person. The dullard needs literal speech; the insightful sees glorification in existence.
This shows that true knowledge goes beyond the literal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا يُؤيد قولَ مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّ الهدى هو العلمُ ; فإِنَّ مَنْ فهم عن الله تعالى فقد اهتدى ، ومَنْ لم يفهم عنِ اللهِ تعالى آياتِهِ فقد ضلَّ وغوى ، وَمِنهُم مَّن يَسْتَمِعُ إِلَيْكَ حَتَّى إِذَا خَرَجُوا مِنْ عِندِكَ قَالُوا لِلَّذِينَ أُوتُوا العلم مَاذَا قَالَ عَائِفاً أُوْلَيكَ الَّذِينَ طَبَعَ اللَّهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ وَاتَّبعوا أَهْوَاءَهُمْ * وَالَّذِينَ اهْتَدَوْا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى وَآتَاهُمْ تَقْوَاهُم ﴾ [محمد : ١٦-١٧] . إحياء علوم الدين ) ( ٣٧٥/١ ) : ( ومن هذا قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَإِن مِّن شَيْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِ ﴾ [الإسراء : ٤٤] ، فإن البليد يفتقر فيه إلى أن يقدر للجماد حياة وعقلاً ونطقاً بصوت وحرف ; حتى يقول : سبحان الله ! ليتحقق تسبيحه ، والبصير يعلم أنه ما أريد به نطق اللسان ، بل كونه مسبحاً بوجوده ، ومقدّساً بذاته ، وشاهداً بوحدانية الله سبحانه ) . فأخبر تعالى أنَّ لهم هداية ، وزادَتْهم الشريعةُ هداية على هدايتهم وآتاهم تقواهم ; أي: أثمرَتْ لهم هدايتهم - وهي علومهم بالله تعالى وبرسوله وبشريعتِهِ - تقویٰ مِنْ عذابِ اللهِ تعالى ، وخوفاً مِنْ عقابِهِ جَلَّ وعز . ولذا قيل : التقوى ثمرة العلم ، والعلم ثمرةُ الفكر ، والفكر نتيجةُ العقلِ ; فمَنْ لم يُرزَقِ العقلَ الحصيفَ حُرِمَ الفكر الباحث ، ومَنْ لم يُرزَق فكراً باحثاً حُرِمَ العلم النافع بالمعقولات ، ومَنْ لم يُرزَق علماً بآيات الله تعالى حُرِمَ العلم بأحكام الله تعالى ، ومَنْ حُرِمَ العلم بأحكام الله تعالى لم يُتصوَّر وجودُ التقوى في قلبه ، وكيفَ يَتَّقِي مَنْ لا يعلمه ؟! وكيف يتركُ لذاتٍ عاجلةً قد عرفها مشاهدةً وذوقاً إلى أمر لم يعلمه إلا تقليداً لآبائِهِ وأهلِ زمانِهِ ، مِنْ غيرِ تحقيق ببرهان ، أو حُجَّةٍ وسلطان ؟!
And this supports the view of those who said: 'Guidance is knowledge; for whoever understands from Allah has been guided, and whoever does not understand Allah's verses has strayed and gone astray.' 'And among them are those who listen to you until when they leave your presence, they say to those who have been given knowledge, 'What did he say just now?' Those are the ones on whose hearts Allah has sealed and who follow their desires.' 'And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance and gives them their piety' [Muhammad 47:16-17]. (Ihya 'Ulum al-Din 1/375): 'And from this is His statement: 'And there is nothing that does not glorify Him with praise' [Al-Isra 17:44]. For the dullard is in need of it to attribute life, intellect, and speech with sound and letter to the inanimate until it says 'Subhan Allah' so that its glorification is realized. But the insightful person knows that what is intended is not the speech of the tongue, but rather its being glorifying by its existence, sanctified by its essence, and witnessing to the oneness of Allah.' So He informed that they have guidance, and the Law increased them in guidance upon their guidance and gave them their piety; meaning: their guidance – which is their knowledge of Allah, His Messenger, and His Law – produced for them piety from the punishment of Allah and fear of His punishment. Hence it is said: 'Piety is the fruit of knowledge, knowledge is the fruit of thought, and thought is the result of intellect.' So whoever is not granted sound intellect is deprived of investigative thought; whoever is not granted investigative thought is deprived of beneficial knowledge of rational matters; whoever is not granted knowledge of Allah's verses is deprived of knowledge of Allah's rulings; and whoever is deprived of knowledge of Allah's rulings, the existence of piety in his heart is inconceivable. How can one fear what he does not know? And how can he abandon immediate pleasures that he has experienced by observation and taste for something he only knows by imitating his fathers and his contemporaries, without verification by proof or evidence and authority?
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a two-part argument. First, Sanusi supports the view that guidance is knowledge, quoting the Quranic verse about those who listen but don't understand and the verse about the guided increasing in guidance and being given taqwa. He then quotes al-Ghazali's Ihya, illustrating that the dullard needs to imagine that inanimate objects speak to affirm God's glory, whereas the insightful person understands that all things glorify God by their very existence. Second, Sanusi explains the verse further: the guidance they had (knowledge of Allah, His Messenger, and His Law) produced taqwa (piety), which is fear of punishment. He then presents the famous hierarchy: taqwa is the fruit of knowledge, knowledge is the fruit of thought, thought is the result of intellect. He then traces the deprivation chain: without sound intellect, no research; without research, no beneficial knowledge of rational matters; without knowledge of Allah's verses, no knowledge of His rulings; without knowledge of rulings, no piety. He concludes with rhetorical questions highlighting the absurdity of fearing what one does not know and the futility of abandoning known pleasures for something known only through imitation without proof.

Key Terms
هدى
علم
تقوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Guidance is merely a feeling or emotional state, separate from knowledge.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly defines guidance as knowledge and understanding from Allah, supported by Quranic verses that tie guidance to comprehension.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the definition of guidance?
A) A feeling of peace in the heart
B) Knowledge and understanding from Allah
C) Following the traditions of one's ancestors
D) Performing religious rituals correctly

Key Takeaway
Guidance is essentially knowledge of Allah, as shown by the Quran and reinforced by the insightful understanding of creation's glorification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever sat through a Quran lesson or sermon, only to walk away unable to recall what was said? Are you like the hypocrites whose hearts are sealed? What will you do this week to ensure you listen with comprehension?
?
The dullard demands that rocks speak with tongues to glorify Allah, but the insightful sees glorification in their very existence. In what areas of your faith do you demand literal proof when Allah has already shown you His signs? Will you ask Him to make you among the insightful?
?
Allah increases the guided in guidance and gives them taqwa. Does your knowledge of Islam draw you closer to Allah and increase your piety? If not, what is the barrier you need to remove today?

The Chain from Intellect to Piety
Sanusi explains the hierarchy from intellect to piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hierarchical relationship between intellect, thought, knowledge, and piety, and why lacking any link in the chain prevents true taqwa.

Core Idea
Piety is the fruit of knowledge, knowledge the fruit of thought, thought the result of intellect.

Building on the previous lesson's identification of guidance with knowledge, Sanusi now expounds a famous hierarchy. He explains that the guidance mentioned in the Quran produces piety because guidance is knowledge of Allah, His Messenger, and His Law. He then presents the chain: piety is the fruit of knowledge, knowledge the fruit of thought, thought the result of intellect. He traces what happens when any link is missing, concluding with rhetorical questions that underscore the necessity of verified knowledge for true fear of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage once to get the overall argument. Notice the hierarchical statements.
This passage is more systematic than the previous one.
2
Identify the hierarchy
Find the line: 'Piety is the fruit of knowledge, knowledge the fruit of thought, thought the result of intellect.' Understand the causal sequence.
This is the core of the lesson.
3
Trace the deprivation chain
Follow Sanusi's negative chain: if one lacks sound intellect, then thought, then knowledge, then knowledge of verses, then knowledge of rulings, then piety is impossible.
Focus on the logical necessity of each link.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical questions
Consider the concluding questions: How can one fear what they don't know? How can one abandon known pleasures for something only known via imitation?
These highlight the absurdity of blind following without knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can attain piety simply by performing rituals or imitating elders, without deep knowledge.

According to the hierarchy presented by Sanusi, what is the direct fruit of thought?
A) Sound intellect
B) Knowledge
C) Piety

Key Takeaway
True piety (taqwa) is built on a foundation of sound intellect, thought, and knowledge; it cannot exist through blind imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a moment to examine your own piety (taqwa). Is it rooted in knowledge you have personally verified through your intellect and thought, or is it largely inherited from your family and community? What step of the chain are you neglecting?
?
If you were to really, honestly investigate the rational basis of your beliefs—starting with your intellect—what aspects of your faith would you need to re-examine? Are you willing to do that even if it means letting go of comfortable assumptions?
?
You have likely been taught to fear Allah, but do you truly know Him through the knowledge of His verses and rulings? How much time do you spend acquiring that knowledge versus merely performing rituals? What is one specific habit you can change today to move from imitation to intellectual conviction?

Warning Against Self-Deception and Evil Scholars
Sanusi warns against self-deception and evil scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the characteristics of the intelligent believer and the dangers of self-deception and evil scholars.

Core Idea
True intelligence is saving your soul through beneficial knowledge and action, not self-delusion.

Sanusi concludes this section with an urgent warning. He defines true intelligence as acting on beneficial knowledge to save oneself from destruction. Then he laments those who are deceived by their own souls into thinking they are perfect without evidence, and those who follow evil scholars. This passage calls for self-examination and sincere reliance on Allah.

Guided Path
1
Define the intelligent person
Read the opening sentence carefully. Notice how Sanusi describes the intelligent person: one whose resolve is stirred to save his soul by acquiring beneficial knowledge and acting upon it.
The Arabic uses 'al-'aqil' for intelligent, implying wisdom, not mere intellect.
2
Identify the two warnings
The passage warns against two things: being deceived by one's own soul (nafs ammara) and being deceived by evil scholars (ulama' al-su'). Find the phrases that express regret and woe.
Note the strong language: 'ya khasara' (what a loss) and 'ya wayha' (woe).
3
Understand the role of the 'shahid'
The passage says the deceived soul imagines perfection in beliefs without any 'shahid' (witness) testifying to that. Reflect on what this witness might be: evidence from revelation and reason.
The shahid is likely proof from the Quran, Sunnah, and sound reasoning.
4
Connect to your own life
Ask yourself: Am I relying on feelings or assumptions about my faith, or do I have solid knowledge and evidence? How can I protect myself from evil scholars?
This lesson is meant to provoke introspection and action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is an admonition and warning. The author defines the intelligent person (al-'aqil) as one whose resolve is activated to save himself from the destruction of the afterlife by acquiring beneficial knowledge (al-'ilm al-nafi') and acting upon it during the brief lifespan which is like a passing shadow. Then he laments the loss of those who listen to the deceptions of the commanding soul (al-nafs al-ammara) which makes them think they are perfect in their beliefs without any witness (shahid) testifying to that. He also warns against the company of evil scholars ('ulama' al-su') described as devils of mankind, leading one to think he is on something while actually perishing without realizing it. The passage ends with a statement that true success is from God alone.

Blind Following in Matters of Decisive Proof
Sanusi argues against excusing taqlid in matters of decisive proof and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why blind following (taqlid) is not an excuse in matters where decisive proof and consensus are established, and how Sanusi defends scholars from false accusations.

Core Idea
Following scholars in error is not excusable when decisive proof and consensus exist.

Sanusi addresses a potential objection: what if a great scholar fell into error? He grants the hypothetical but insists that following him in that error is still not excusable. This is because matters of creed are based on decisive proof and consensus, not on authority. He also dismisses false accusations against reputable scholars. This lesson clarifies the limits of taqlid in theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let the author's reasoning unfold naturally before analyzing.
Pay attention to the hypothetical 'if it were supposed'.
2
Analyze the hypothetical concession
Notice that Sanusi grants a hypothetical scenario for the sake of argument. Understand the rhetorical technique: even if we assume error occurred, it does not justify following it.
This is a common kalam method to strengthen a point.
3
Understand the principle and the defense
Identify the principle that taqlid in creed matters with consensus on correctness is not sufficient, especially when decisive proof shows corruption. Also see how Sanusi dismisses slander against scholars.
The passage refutes both the justification of error and the false accusations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قُدِّرَ أنَّ ذلكَ وقعَ منه - رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه ـ على سبيلِ الفَرْضِ والتسليمِ الجدليّ كما يُقدَّرُ وقوع المحالِ ، ولا حول ولا قوَّةَ إلا بالله العلي العظيم .. لم يكن لهم عذر ولا حُجَّةٌ باتباعِهِ(١) ; إذ التقليد في عقائد الدين المجمع على صحتها لا يفيد عندَ كثيرٍ مِنَ المحققينَ فكيف بالتقليد فيما قام البرهان القطعي وحصل الإجماع على فسادِهِ ؟!(٢) وما يُوجَدُ في بعض التآليف ; مِنْ تلطيخ الشيخ ابن أبي زيد ) . وأبي عمرَ بنِ عبدِ البرّ وبعض السلفِ بهِ (٣). . ففاسد لا يُلتفتُ إليهِ.
And if it were supposed that that occurred from him - may Allah be pleased with him - by way of hypothetical assumption and dialectical concession, just as the occurrence of the impossible is supposed, and there is no power and no strength except by Allah, the Most High, the Almighty - they would have no excuse or proof in following him; for blind imitation (taqlid) in the creeds of the religion on whose correctness there is consensus does not avail according to many of the verifiers, so how about blind imitation in that for which definitive proof has been established and consensus has been reached on its corruption?! And what is found in some works, of smearing of Sheikh Ibn Abi Zayd and Abu 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-Barr and some of the Salaf with it - it is corrupt and not to be paid attention to.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is both a refutation of an objection and a statement of principle. The author begins by granting a hypothetical: even if it were supposed that a great scholar (presumably Imam Ahmad or another) actually said or did something problematic, by way of hypothetical concession for the sake of argument, that would still not excuse anyone following him in that error. The reason: blind imitation (taqlid) in matters of creed where there is consensus on correctness is already considered insufficient by many verifiers. How much more so when there is definitive proof and consensus that the position in question is corrupt. Then the author responds to a charge: some works smear Ibn Abi Zayd, Ibn 'Abd al-Barr, and some Salaf with anthropomorphism. The author dismisses these charges as corrupt and unworthy of attention. The key point: authority does not justify error, and slandering reputable scholars with false accusations is itself corrupt.

Key Terms
تقليد
برهان قطعي
إجماع
اتباع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that following a revered scholar justifies accepting error.
Correction: Sanusi argues that even if a great scholar made an error, following him in that error is not excusable, especially when decisive proof and consensus show the error.

Checkpoint

A) It is allowed because of his status
B) It is not excusable
C) It is obligatory to follow him
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Blind imitation (taqlid) does not excuse error when decisive proof and consensus are clear, and slander against scholars is corrupt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever defended a personal belief only because a scholar you love held it, without checking the decisive proof yourself? What will you do now to change that?
?
You have probably heard negative things about some scholars from the Salaf. The passage calls such smears 'corrupt'. Will you investigate such claims before repeating them, or will you commit to silence?
?
Which of your core beliefs do you hold based on taqlid rather than certainty? Are you willing to examine each one under the light of decisive proof, no matter the cost?

The Two Ignorances of Iblis: Content and Refutation
Sanusi enumerates and refutes the two ignorances of Iblis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two theological errors that Sanusi identifies as the root of Iblis's rebellion and the orthodox Sunni refutation of each.

Core Idea
Iblis's sin was rooted in specific doctrinal errors, not just pride.

Sanusi begins by revealing that even Iblis's long worship was tainted by two fundamental ignorances. These are not minor mistakes but doctrinal deviations that contradict the core beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah. In this lesson, we examine each ignorance and why it is false.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage twice
First read the Arabic and translation to get the flow. Then reread to identify the two ignorances.
Notice that Sanusi labels the first a 'philosophical ignorance' and the second 'the ignorance of the Qadariyya'.
2
Understand the first ignorance
Iblis believed bodies differ in excellence by their own natures. Sanusi refutes this by stating all bodies are equal in essence and only God gives preference.
3
Understand the second ignorance
Iblis believed the servant's power has an effect in actions and that God must do what is beneficial. Sanusi refutes this by affirming that God alone creates all actions and is not obligated.
This is the Qadariyya doctrine.
4
Reflect on the refutations
Consider how each refutation connects to core Sunni beliefs: tawhid and divine omnipotence.
The first ignorance undermines tawhid; the second undermines divine sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد قيل : إنَّ الشيطان قد عبد الله تعالى ثمانين ألف سنةٍ لا يفتر، لكن قد صحبَهُ في عبادتِهِ جهالتانِ كُتبتا عليهِ في الأزلِ، ولا حول ولا قوَّةَ إلا بالله العلي العظيم ، وهما أمارتا شقاوته : إحداهما : أنَّ الأجسامَ كانَتْ عندَهُ متفاضلة بطباعها : وهي جهالة فلسفية لا ثبوت لها على مذهب المؤمنينَ، وإِنَّما العالم كله عندهم أجسام وصفاتُ أجسام، لا فضل لبعضه على بعضٍ مِنْ حيثُ ذاتُهُ، فيُخصِّصُ الله تعالى أي جسم شاءَ بأي صفةٍ شاءَ، ويُبدِّلُ الحار بارداً، والمنير مظلماً، والحيَّ ميتاً إلى غير ذلك، فالأجسام ظروف وأوعيةٌ للصفاتِ، ومولانا جلَّ وعزَّ مختار لكلِّ ظرف منها ما يجعلُ فيهِ، فلا أفضليَّةَ لجسم على آخرَ إلا بتفضيله سبحانه وتعالى الجهالة الثانيةُ : أَنَّهُ كانَ يعتقد أنَّ قدرة العبدِ لها أثر في الأفعالِ وأنَّ العبد إنَّما يطيع الله تعالى أو يعصيه بقدرتِهِ ومشيئتِهِ هو، لا أنَّ اللهَ تعالى هو الذي يخلقُ الطاعة والمعصية، ونشأ لهُ مِنْ هذه الجهالة اعتقاد وجوبِ مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح على الله تعالى، وهذه جهالة القدريّة مجوس هذه الأمة ولا جريان لها على مذهب أهل السنة المتبرتينَ مِنَ الحولِ والقوَّةِ، والمفوضين جميع الأمور إلى الله تعالى، لا يرونَ معَهُ جل وعزَّ شريكاً في ملكه، ولا مؤثراً سواه في أثرٍ ما على العموم، لا بطبعه ولا بخاصية جُعِلَتْ فيهِ ولأجلِ كُمون هاتين الجهالتين في باطن إبليس ، وانطواء عقدِهِ عليهما لما خلق الله آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ مِنَ التراب، وهو المفضولُ عندَ إبليس اللعين بالنسبة إلى النار التي خُلِقَ هو منها، ثم أُمِرَ في جملة الملائكة بالسجودِ لآدمَ والتعظيمِ القَدْرِهِ، ولم تتقدَّمْ مِنْ آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ عبادةٌ . . أَنفَ إبليس - لعنَهُ اللهُ - وعظم أصله وعبادته؛ إذ رأى نفسَه فاعلاً لها، وَجوَّرَ مولانا جل وعزّ في حُكمِهِ عليهِ بالسجودِ لآدمَ عليه السلام والتواضع له، وجاهرَهُ عزَّ وجلَّ بقولِهِ : أَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ [الأعراف : 12] ، وبقوله : أَرَعَيْنَكَ هَذَا الَّذِي كَرَّمْتَ عَلَى [الإسراء : 62] !
It has been said: Indeed, the devil worshipped God Almighty for eighty thousand years without slackening, but two ignorances accompanied him in his worship, written upon him in pre-eternity. There is no power and no strength except with God the Most High, the Almighty, and they are the two marks of his wretchedness: The first of them: that bodies were in his view differing in excellence by their natures – and this is a philosophical ignorance that has no basis in the creed of the believers. Rather, the whole world according to them is bodies and attributes of bodies, no part having superiority over another in terms of its essence. God Almighty particularizes any body He wills with any attribute He wills, and changes hot to cold, luminous to dark, living to dead, and so on. Thus bodies are containers and vessels for attributes, and our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, is the Chooser for each container of what He places in it. So there is no superiority of one body over another except by His, Exalted and High, bestowing preference. The second ignorance: that he believed that the servant's power has an effect in actions, and that the servant obeys God Almighty or disobeys Him by his own power and will, not that God Almighty is the One who creates obedience and disobedience. From this ignorance arose for him the belief in the obligation of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial upon God Almighty. And this is the ignorance of the Qadariyya, the Magians of this community. And it has no currency in the doctrine of the People of the Sunnah, who absolve themselves from power and strength and delegate all matters to God Almighty, seeing no partner with Him, Mighty and Majestic, in His dominion, nor any agent other than Him in any effect whatsoever, generally, neither by its nature nor by a property placed in it. And because of the concealment of these two ignorances in the inner being of Iblis and the enfolding of his knot upon them – when God created Adam, peace be upon him, from dust, while he was, according to accursed Iblis, inferior to the fire from which he himself was created – then he was commanded among the company of angels to prostrate to Adam and magnify his worth, and no worship had preceded from Adam, peace be upon him. Iblis – may God curse him – became disdainful, and considered great his origin and his worship, since he saw himself as the doer of it, and he deemed our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, unjust in His command to him to prostrate to Adam and humble himself before him, and he openly confronted Him, Mighty and Majestic, with His words: 'I am better than him' [Al-A'raf: 12], and with His words: 'Do You see this one whom You have honored above me?' [Al-Isra': 62]!
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage explains the two ignorances (جهالتان) that accompanied Iblis (Satan) in his long worship of God, which ultimately led to his refusal to prostrate to Adam and his rebellion. Sanusi begins by noting that Iblis worshipped God for eighty thousand years without slackening, but two ignorances were written upon him in pre-eternity and marked his wretchedness. He then enumerates them:

1) The first ignorance: the belief that bodies differ in excellence by their own natures (متفاضلة بطباعها). Sanusi labels this a philosophical ignorance (جهالة فلسفية) that contradicts the creed of the believers. According to Ahl al-Sunnah, all bodies are equal in their essence; they are mere containers (ظروف) and vessels (أوعية) for attributes. God has absolute freedom to assign any attribute to any body, so no body is inherently superior to another except by God's choosing. This ignorance led Iblis to consider fire superior to clay, hence his disdain for Adam who was created from clay.

2) The second ignorance: the belief that the servant's power (قدرة العبد) has an actual effect in actions, and that the servant obeys or disobeys by his own power and will, not that God creates both obedience and disobedience. From this, Iblis concluded that God is obligated to observe what is beneficial and most beneficial (الصلاح والأصلح) for His creatures – a doctrine of the Qadariyya (deniers of divine decree), whom Sanusi calls 'the Magians of this community'. This is rejected by Ahl al-Sunnah, who delegate all matters to God and affirm that no effect occurs except by His will and power.

Sanusi then explains how these two ignorances caused Iblis's rebellion when Adam was created. Because Iblis held that fire (his origin) is superior to clay (Adam's origin) by nature, and that his own worship was his own doing, he became arrogant when commanded to prostrate to Adam. He deemed God's command unjust (جوَّر) and openly declared, 'I am better than him' and 'Do You see this one whom You have honored above me?' Thus, the two ignorances are presented as the doctrinal roots of his disobedience.

Key Terms
جهالتان
متفاضلة بطباعها
جهالة فلسفية
قدرة العبد
صلاح وأصلح
قدريّة
مجوس هذه الأمة
أهل السنة
مفوضين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iblis's sin was simply arrogance and pride.
Correction: Sanusi shows that his sin was rooted in two specific theological ignorances: belief in inherent superiority of bodies and belief in servant's independent power.

Checkpoint
What is the first ignorance of Iblis according to Sanusi?
A) That bodies differ in excellence by their natures
B) That God is unjust
C) That worship is unnecessary
D) That angels are superior to humans

Key Takeaway
Iblis's rebellion was not merely a moral failure but stemmed from specific doctrinal errors that contradict the foundations of Sunni belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your acts of worship—prayer, charity, fasting—do you ever feel that your own effort and will are the true cause of your piety? Iblis's second ignorance was believing his power had an effect. Ask yourself: in what area of your life are you relying on your own strength rather than God's creation of your actions? Write down one concrete step to surrender that self-sufficiency today.
?
You may judge others based on their appearance, wealth, or status, as if those qualities are inherent excellences. The first ignorance of Iblis was precisely this: thinking bodies differ by nature. How does this passage confront the way you view others? Will you commit to seeing every person as a vessel that God has filled with attributes—and therefore worthy of respect regardless of their outward station?
?
Iblis worshipped for 80,000 years, yet his ignorances nullified it. What false beliefs about God's attributes or your own capacity might be lurking in your heart, slowly poisoning your devotion? Take a moment to identify one such belief—however subtle—and pray for the knowledge to see it and the courage to uproot it.

How the Ignorances Led to Iblis's Rebellion
Sanusi narrates Iblis's rebellion as the practical consequence of his two ignorances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the two ignorances manifested in Iblis's refusal to prostrate to Adam and his direct confrontation with God.

Core Idea
The ignorances turned Iblis from a long-time worshipper into an open rebel against God's command.

Having identified the two ignorances, Sanusi now shows how they played out when God commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam. Iblis's hidden errors surfaced, leading him to arrogance, accusation of injustice against God, and open defiance.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative of rebellion
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the sequence: creation of Adam, command to prostrate, Iblis's reaction.
Notice the connective 'because of the concealment' links back to the ignorances.
2
Connect first ignorance to disdain
Iblis considered Adam inferior because he was from dust, while Iblis was from fire. This stems from the first ignorance about inherent superiority of bodies.
He 'considered great his origin' (fire).
3
Connect second ignorance to accusation
Iblis saw his own worship as his doing, so he deemed God's command unfair. This stems from the second ignorance about servant's power.
He 'deemed our Lord unjust in His command'.
4
Observe his final statements
Iblis openly says 'I am better than him' and 'Do You see this one whom You have honored above me?' These reflect both ignorances.
The Quranic verses are cited as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد قيل : إنَّ الشيطان قد عبد الله تعالى ثمانين ألف سنةٍ لا يفتر، لكن قد صحبَهُ في عبادتِهِ جهالتانِ كُتبتا عليهِ في الأزلِ، ولا حول ولا قوَّةَ إلا بالله العلي العظيم ، وهما أمارتا شقاوته : إحداهما : أنَّ الأجسامَ كانَتْ عندَهُ متفاضلة بطباعها : وهي جهالة فلسفية لا ثبوت لها على مذهب المؤمنينَ، وإِنَّما العالم كله عندهم أجسام وصفاتُ أجسام، لا فضل لبعضه على بعضٍ مِنْ حيثُ ذاتُهُ، فيُخصِّصُ الله تعالى أي جسم شاءَ بأي صفةٍ شاءَ، ويُبدِّلُ الحار بارداً، والمنير مظلماً، والحيَّ ميتاً إلى غير ذلك، فالأجسام ظروف وأوعيةٌ للصفاتِ، ومولانا جلَّ وعزَّ مختار لكلِّ ظرف منها ما يجعلُ فيهِ، فلا أفضليَّةَ لجسم على آخرَ إلا بتفضيله سبحانه وتعالى الجهالة الثانيةُ : أَنَّهُ كانَ يعتقد أنَّ قدرة العبدِ لها أثر في الأفعالِ وأنَّ العبد إنَّما يطيع الله تعالى أو يعصيه بقدرتِهِ ومشيئتِهِ هو، لا أنَّ اللهَ تعالى هو الذي يخلقُ الطاعة والمعصية، ونشأ لهُ مِنْ هذه الجهالة اعتقاد وجوبِ مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح على الله تعالى، وهذه جهالة القدريّة مجوس هذه الأمة ولا جريان لها على مذهب أهل السنة المتبرتينَ مِنَ الحولِ والقوَّةِ، والمفوضين جميع الأمور إلى الله تعالى، لا يرونَ معَهُ جل وعزَّ شريكاً في ملكه، ولا مؤثراً سواه في أثرٍ ما على العموم، لا بطبعه ولا بخاصية جُعِلَتْ فيهِ ولأجلِ كُمون هاتين الجهالتين في باطن إبليس ، وانطواء عقدِهِ عليهما لما خلق الله آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ مِنَ التراب، وهو المفضولُ عندَ إبليس اللعين بالنسبة إلى النار التي خُلِقَ هو منها، ثم أُمِرَ في جملة الملائكة بالسجودِ لآدمَ والتعظيمِ القَدْرِهِ، ولم تتقدَّمْ مِنْ آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ عبادةٌ . . أَنفَ إبليس - لعنَهُ اللهُ - وعظم أصله وعبادته؛ إذ رأى نفسَه فاعلاً لها، وَجوَّرَ مولانا جل وعزّ في حُكمِهِ عليهِ بالسجودِ لآدمَ عليه السلام والتواضع له، وجاهرَهُ عزَّ وجلَّ بقولِهِ : أَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ [الأعراف : 12] ، وبقوله : أَرَعَيْنَكَ هَذَا الَّذِي كَرَّمْتَ عَلَى [الإسراء : 62] !
It has been said: Indeed, the devil worshipped God Almighty for eighty thousand years without slackening, but two ignorances accompanied him in his worship, written upon him in pre-eternity. There is no power and no strength except with God the Most High, the Almighty, and they are the two marks of his wretchedness: The first of them: that bodies were in his view differing in excellence by their natures – and this is a philosophical ignorance that has no basis in the creed of the believers. Rather, the whole world according to them is bodies and attributes of bodies, no part having superiority over another in terms of its essence. God Almighty particularizes any body He wills with any attribute He wills, and changes hot to cold, luminous to dark, living to dead, and so on. Thus bodies are containers and vessels for attributes, and our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, is the Chooser for each container of what He places in it. So there is no superiority of one body over another except by His, Exalted and High, bestowing preference. The second ignorance: that he believed that the servant's power has an effect in actions, and that the servant obeys God Almighty or disobeys Him by his own power and will, not that God Almighty is the One who creates obedience and disobedience. From this ignorance arose for him the belief in the obligation of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial upon God Almighty. And this is the ignorance of the Qadariyya, the Magians of this community. And it has no currency in the doctrine of the People of the Sunnah, who absolve themselves from power and strength and delegate all matters to God Almighty, seeing no partner with Him, Mighty and Majestic, in His dominion, nor any agent other than Him in any effect whatsoever, generally, neither by its nature nor by a property placed in it. And because of the concealment of these two ignorances in the inner being of Iblis and the enfolding of his knot upon them – when God created Adam, peace be upon him, from dust, while he was, according to accursed Iblis, inferior to the fire from which he himself was created – then he was commanded among the company of angels to prostrate to Adam and magnify his worth, and no worship had preceded from Adam, peace be upon him. Iblis – may God curse him – became disdainful, and considered great his origin and his worship, since he saw himself as the doer of it, and he deemed our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, unjust in His command to him to prostrate to Adam and humble himself before him, and he openly confronted Him, Mighty and Majestic, with His words: 'I am better than him' [Al-A'raf: 12], and with His words: 'Do You see this one whom You have honored above me?' [Al-Isra': 62]!
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage explains the two ignorances (جهالتان) that accompanied Iblis (Satan) in his long worship of God, which ultimately led to his refusal to prostrate to Adam and his rebellion. Sanusi begins by noting that Iblis worshipped God for eighty thousand years without slackening, but two ignorances were written upon him in pre-eternity and marked his wretchedness. He then enumerates them:

1) The first ignorance: the belief that bodies differ in excellence by their own natures (متفاضلة بطباعها). Sanusi labels this a philosophical ignorance (جهالة فلسفية) that contradicts the creed of the believers. According to Ahl al-Sunnah, all bodies are equal in their essence; they are mere containers (ظروف) and vessels (أوعية) for attributes. God has absolute freedom to assign any attribute to any body, so no body is inherently superior to another except by God's choosing. This ignorance led Iblis to consider fire superior to clay, hence his disdain for Adam who was created from clay.

2) The second ignorance: the belief that the servant's power (قدرة العبد) has an actual effect in actions, and that the servant obeys or disobeys by his own power and will, not that God creates both obedience and disobedience. From this, Iblis concluded that God is obligated to observe what is beneficial and most beneficial (الصلاح والأصلح) for His creatures – a doctrine of the Qadariyya (deniers of divine decree), whom Sanusi calls 'the Magians of this community'. This is rejected by Ahl al-Sunnah, who delegate all matters to God and affirm that no effect occurs except by His will and power.

Sanusi then explains how these two ignorances caused Iblis's rebellion when Adam was created. Because Iblis held that fire (his origin) is superior to clay (Adam's origin) by nature, and that his own worship was his own doing, he became arrogant when commanded to prostrate to Adam. He deemed God's command unjust (جوَّر) and openly declared, 'I am better than him' and 'Do You see this one whom You have honored above me?' Thus, the two ignorances are presented as the doctrinal roots of his disobedience.

Key Terms
كُمون
انطواء عقد
أَنف
جوَّر
أَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ
أَرَعَيْنَكَ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iblis refused to prostrate simply because he was jealous or proud without any doctrinal basis.
Correction: Sanusi shows that his refusal was directly caused by two specific theological errors about the nature of bodies and the power of the servant.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why did Iblis consider himself better than Adam?
A) Because he was created from fire
B) Because he had worshipped longer
C) Because he was an angel
D) Because he had more knowledge

Key Takeaway
Iblis's rebellion is a direct consequence of his erroneous beliefs about the nature of bodies and the power of the servant.
