The Humility of the Angels and Their Reliance on Grace
Sanusi describes the angels' humility and their recognition of divine grace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the angels humbly attribute all their virtues and worship to Allah's grace alone, recognizing no inherent merit in themselves.

Core Idea
Angels see themselves as zeroes; only Allah's grace gives them value.

Sanusi begins by describing the profound humility of the angels. Despite their exalted status and immense worship, they do not rely on their own light or actions. Instead, they recognize that everything they have is pure gift from Allah. This lesson unpacks their mindset and the Quranic verse that confirms their universal prostration.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the angels' attitude
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice how the author describes the angels' disregard for their own light and worship.
The passage contrasts angels' humility with potential pride.
2
Identify why the angels ignore their own light
The author states that the angels' special status is only by Allah's pure grace, not by their nature. They see their light and others as equal before Allah.
3
Understand why they ignore their worship
They consider worship as Allah's action without mediation, so they see no effect from themselves. They stand equal with Adam in not creating any worship.
This shows extreme humility.
4
Reflect on the emphatic wording of the prostration verse
Allah used both 'kulluhum' and 'ajma‘un' to emphasize that all angels prostrated, removing any surprise at the universal obedience.
This confirms the angels' complete submission.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَمَّلَهم لخطاب تكليفِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ (۱)، ولم يلتفتوا إلى النور الذي هو أصلهم؛ إذ هو وغيره سواءٌ. واختصاصُهُ بما اختص بهِ إنَّما هو بمخض فضل الله تعالى، لا بطبعه، فروا عليهم السلامُ أنَّ ذلكَ ممَّا يُوجِبُ غرقهم في بحارِ أَنْعُمِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ؛ إِذْ حَصَّهم مِنَ النِّعَمِ الجليلة بلا استحقاق منهم لشيء منها عليه تعالى بما لم يعطِهِ غيرَهم، وهو القادر سبحانَهُ أنْ يجعلَ الترابَ مضيئاً ونوراً، ويجعل النور مظلماً. وكذا لم يلتفتوا أيضاً عليهم السلام إلى ما مضى منهم مِنْ عظيمِ العبادة؛ إذ هي فعْلُ اللهِ تعالى بلا واسطةٍ، فلم يرَوا لأنفسهم تأثيراً ألبتةَ، فهم وآدمُ عليهِ السلامُ في عدم إيجاد شيء مِنَ العبادة سواء، ولهذا قال تعالى مادحاً لهم بما وفقهم له سبحانَهُ مِنْ حُسْنِ الاعتقادِ والامتثال بمحْضِ فضلِهِ: ﴿ فَسَجَدَ الْمَلائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ ﴾ [ص: ٧٣]، فوَكَّدَ تعالى تعميم السجودِ في جميعهم بـ (كل) و (أجمع) بعد ما أتى بصيغة العموم في قوله: ﴿ الْمَلائِكَةُ ﴾، دَفْعاً لما يُستغربَ مِنْ وقوع السجودِ مِنْ جميعهم مع كثرتهم جداً كثرةً تخرج عن الحصر. عسى أن والله سبحانه وتعالى يتفضَّلُ على مَنْ شاءَ بالكرامة العظمى؛ وهي كرامة الاستقامة في الظاهر والباطن، ويعدلُ فيمَنْ شَاءَ؛ فيَحْتِمُ عليهِ الشقاوة والخلود في أليم العذابِ، ولا يشرح صدرَهُ لحُسْنِ المعرفةِ به تعالى. ورُبَّما أطلقَ تعالى مجرَّدَ الجوارحِ للعبادة مع انطواء القلبِ مِنْ صاحبها على فسادٍ في الاعتقادِ، فتكون تلك الأعمالُ كلُّها هباءً منثوراً، وليس لصاحبها منها إلا مجرَّدُ التعب، كما فعل بإبليس اللعين في مُدَّة ثمانين ألف سنة التي عبد الله فيها لا يفتر، ولم ينفعه الله بشيء منها، وهذا شأنُ مَنْ لم يعتنِ بمعرفةِ أوَّلِ واجب عليه؛ وهو علم التوحيدِ، قالَ اللهُ تعالى: ﴿ وَقَدِمْنَا إِلَى مَا عَمِلُوا مِنْ عَمَلٍ فَجَعَلْنَاهُ هَبَاءً مَنْثُورًا ﴾ [الفرقان: ٢٣]، وقال جل وعزَّ: ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا أَعْمَالُهُمْ كَسَرَابٍ بِقِيعَةٍ يَحْسَبُهُ الظَّمْآنُ مَاءً حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءَهُ لَمْ يَجِدْهُ شَيْئًا وَوَجَدَ اللَّهَ عِنْدَهُ فَوَفَّاهُ حِسَابَهُ وَاللَّهُ سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ ﴾ [النور: ٣٩]. نسأله سبحانَهُ حُسْنَ المعرفةِ بهِ، وألا يحرمنا مِنْ عظيم فضلِهِ، وأنْ يَمُنَّ علينا بحُسْنِ الخاتمة والمغفرة لجميع الذنوب بلا محنة دنيا وأخرى.
He inclined them to the address of His obligation, Exalted and Majestic (1), and they did not pay attention to the light which is their origin; for it and other than it are equal. And his specialization with what he specialized with is only by the pure grace of Allah the Exalted, not by his nature. So they fled, peace be upon them, that that causes them to drown in the seas of His blessings, Exalted and Majestic; since He granted them from the great blessings without any merit from them for anything of that, over the Exalted, with what He did not give to others. And He is the Able, Glorious, to make dust luminous and light, and to make light dark. Likewise, they did not pay attention, peace be upon them, to what passed from them of great worship; for it is the action of Allah the Exalted without mediation, so they did not see for themselves any effect at all. So they and Adam, peace be upon him, are equal in not creating anything of worship. And for this, the Exalted said, praising them for what He, Glorious, granted them of good belief and compliance by His pure grace: {So the angels prostrated, all of them together} [Sad: 73]. So the Exalted emphasized the generality of the prostration among all of them with 'every' and 'all' after bringing the general form in His saying: {the angels}, to repel what would be wondered at from the occurrence of prostration from all of them, despite their very great number, a number beyond enumeration. Perhaps that, and Allah the Glorious and Exalted bestows upon whom He wills the greatest honor, which is the honor of uprightness in the outward and inward, and He is just with whom He wills, so He decrees for him misery and eternity in painful punishment, and He does not expand his breast for good knowledge of Him. And sometimes the Exalted merely sets the limbs in motion for worship while the heart of its owner is wrapped in corruption of belief, so those deeds become all scattered dust, and its owner has nothing from them except mere fatigue, as He did with Iblis the accursed in the period of eighty thousand years in which he worshipped Allah without ceasing, and Allah did not benefit him with anything from it. And this is the condition of one who does not care for knowledge of the first obligation upon him, which is the science of tawhid. Allah the Exalted said: {And We shall advance to what they have done of deeds and make them scattered dust} [Al-Furqan: 23], and He said, Exalted and Majestic: {And those who disbelieve, their deeds are like a mirage in a desert which the thirsty supposes is water until when he comes to it he finds it nothing and finds Allah with him, so He pays him his account in full; and Allah is swift in reckoning} [An-Nur: 39]. We ask Him, Glorious, for good knowledge of Him, and that He not deprive us of His great bounty, and that He bestow upon us a good ending and forgiveness for all sins without trial in this world or the next.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument and warning. It begins by describing the angels' attitude: they do not rely on their own essence or worship but recognize everything as pure grace from Allah. The author explains that even their special status is by divine favor, not inherent merit. They see their worship as Allah's act, so they claim no effect for themselves—standing equal with Adam in this regard. Then the author cites the verse of universal prostration (Sad: 73), noting the emphatic wording to remove any surprise that all angels prostrated. The passage then shifts: Allah grants uprightness to whom He wills and decrees misery for others. The key warning follows: mere physical worship without correct belief is worthless, like Iblis's eighty thousand years of worship which profited him nothing because he lacked tawhid. The author cites Quranic verses (Al-Furqan: 23, An-Nur: 39) to support that actions of disbelievers are wasted. The passage concludes with a prayer for sound knowledge of Allah, forgiveness, and a good end.

نور
استحقاق
عبادة
سجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are inherently superior and have earned their high rank through their own nature or worship.
Correction: Sanusi explains that the angels' specialization is only by Allah's pure grace, not by their nature, and they do not rely on their worship at all.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the angels not rely on their worship?
A) Because their worship is insignificant.
B) Because they see worship as Allah's act without mediation.
C) Because they want to be humble.
D) Because they are equal to Adam.

Key Takeaway
Angels recognize that all their virtues and worship are pure gifts from Allah, so they remain humble and claim no merit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels saw their own worship as Allah's act with no effect from themselves. When you perform good deeds, do you subtly attribute them to your own effort or righteousness? Can you sincerely say that your worship is not from you but from Allah?
?
If you truly believed that every virtue you have is by Allah's pure grace with no merit from you, how would your attitude change toward your own achievements and toward others who have less? What would you stop feeling proud of?
?
The angels and Adam are equal in not creating worship. Do you ever look down on others because you think your worship is better or more acceptable? How would you treat your own acts of worship if you saw them as merely Allah's gift to you, not your own offering to Him?

The Danger of Actions Without Correct Belief
Sanusi warns that actions without correct belief are wasted, using Iblis as an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why deeds performed without correct belief (tawhid) are worthless, using the example of Iblis and Quranic proofs.

Core Idea
Worship without correct belief is like scattered dust.

After discussing the angels' humility, Sanusi turns to a stern warning. He explains that Allah grants uprightness to whom He wills, and that mere physical worship without sound belief is futile. The example of Iblis—who worshipped for eighty thousand years—shows that deeds without tawhid are rejected. The lesson also includes Quranic evidence and a prayer for sound knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning about Allah's will and uprightness
Sanusi states that Allah bestows the honor of uprightness on whom He wills and decrees misery on others. This sets the context that guidance comes from Allah.
The phrase 'la yashrah sadrahu' indicates spiritual openness.
2
Note the condition of the heart while performing worship
The author warns that sometimes the limbs are engaged in worship but the heart is corrupt in belief. Such deeds become scattered dust.
This highlights the primacy of correct belief.
3
Examine the example of Iblis
Iblis worshipped for eighty thousand years without ceasing, but it profited him nothing because he lacked correct belief (tawhid).
This is the key example of wasted deeds.
4
Reflect on the Quranic verses about wasted deeds
Sanusi cites Al-Furqan 23 and An-Nur 39, showing that deeds of disbelievers are like scattered dust or a mirage.
These verses reinforce the warning.

على مَنْ شاءَ بالكرامة العظمى؛ وهي كرامة الاستقامة في الظاهر والباطن، ويعدلُ فيمَنْ شَاءَ؛ فيَحْتِمُ عليهِ الشقاوة والخلود في أليم العذابِ، ولا يشرح صدرَهُ لحُسْنِ المعرفةِ به تعالى. ورُبَّما أطلقَ تعالى مجرَّدَ الجوارحِ للعبادة مع انطواء القلبِ مِنْ صاحبها على فسادٍ في الاعتقادِ، فتكون تلك الأعمالُ كلُّها هباءً منثوراً، وليس لصاحبها منها إلا مجرَّدُ التعب، كما فعل بإبليس اللعين في مُدَّة ثمانين ألف سنة التي عبد الله فيها لا يفتر، ولم ينفعه الله بشيء منها، وهذا شأنُ مَنْ لم يعتنِ بمعرفةِ أوَّلِ واجب عليه؛ وهو علم التوحيدِ، قالَ اللهُ تعالى: ﴿ وَقَدِمْنَا إِلَى مَا عَمِلُوا مِنْ عَمَلٍ فَجَعَلْنَاهُ هَبَاءً مَنْثُورًا ﴾ [الفرقان: ٢٣]، وقال جل وعزَّ: ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا أَعْمَالُهُمْ كَسَرَابٍ بِقِيعَةٍ يَحْسَبُهُ الظَّمْآنُ مَاءً حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءَهُ لَمْ يَجِدْهُ شَيْئًا وَوَجَدَ اللَّهَ عِنْدَهُ فَوَفَّاهُ حِسَابَهُ وَاللَّهُ سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ ﴾ [النور: ٣٩]. نسأله سبحانَهُ حُسْنَ المعرفةِ بهِ، وألا يحرمنا مِنْ عظيم فضلِهِ، وأنْ يَمُنَّ علينا بحُسْنِ الخاتمة والمغفرة لجميع الذنوب بلا محنة دنيا وأخرى.
He inclined them to the address of His obligation, Exalted and Majestic (1), and they did not pay attention to the light which is their origin; for it and other than it are equal. And his specialization with what he specialized with is only by the pure grace of Allah the Exalted, not by his nature. So they fled, peace be upon them, that that causes them to drown in the seas of His blessings, Exalted and Majestic; since He granted them from the great blessings without any merit from them for anything of that, over the Exalted, with what He did not give to others. And He is the Able, Glorious, to make dust luminous and light, and to make light dark. Likewise, they did not pay attention, peace be upon them, to what passed from them of great worship; for it is the action of Allah the Exalted without mediation, so they did not see for themselves any effect at all. So they and Adam, peace be upon him, are equal in not creating anything of worship. And for this, the Exalted said, praising them for what He, Glorious, granted them of good belief and compliance by His pure grace: {So the angels prostrated, all of them together} [Sad: 73]. So the Exalted emphasized the generality of the prostration among all of them with 'every' and 'all' after bringing the general form in His saying: {the angels}, to repel what would be wondered at from the occurrence of prostration from all of them, despite their very great number, a number beyond enumeration. Perhaps that, and Allah the Glorious and Exalted bestows upon whom He wills the greatest honor, which is the honor of uprightness in the outward and inward, and He is just with whom He wills, so He decrees for him misery and eternity in painful punishment, and He does not expand his breast for good knowledge of Him. And sometimes the Exalted merely sets the limbs in motion for worship while the heart of its owner is wrapped in corruption of belief, so those deeds become all scattered dust, and its owner has nothing from them except mere fatigue, as He did with Iblis the accursed in the period of eighty thousand years in which he worshipped Allah without ceasing, and Allah did not benefit him with anything from it. And this is the condition of one who does not care for knowledge of the first obligation upon him, which is the science of tawhid. Allah the Exalted said: {And We shall advance to what they have done of deeds and make them scattered dust} [Al-Furqan: 23], and He said, Exalted and Majestic: {And those who disbelieve, their deeds are like a mirage in a desert which the thirsty supposes is water until when he comes to it he finds it nothing and finds Allah with him, so He pays him his account in full; and Allah is swift in reckoning} [An-Nur: 39]. We ask Him, Glorious, for good knowledge of Him, and that He not deprive us of His great bounty, and that He bestow upon us a good ending and forgiveness for all sins without trial in this world or the next.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument and warning. It begins by describing the angels' attitude: they do not rely on their own essence or worship but recognize everything as pure grace from Allah. The author explains that even their special status is by divine favor, not inherent merit. They see their worship as Allah's act, so they claim no effect for themselves—standing equal with Adam in this regard. Then the author cites the verse of universal prostration (Sad: 73), noting the emphatic wording to remove any surprise that all angels prostrated. The passage then shifts: Allah grants uprightness to whom He wills and decrees misery for others. The key warning follows: mere physical worship without correct belief is worthless, like Iblis's eighty thousand years of worship which profited him nothing because he lacked tawhid. The author cites Quranic verses (Al-Furqan: 23, An-Nur: 39) to support that actions of disbelievers are wasted. The passage concludes with a prayer for sound knowledge of Allah, forgiveness, and a good end.

Key Terms

هباء منثورًا
سراب
إبليس
علم التوحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Performing many acts of worship guarantees their acceptance.
Correction: Sanusi shows that Iblis worshipped for 80,000 years but it profited him nothing because his belief was corrupt.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about Iblis's eighty thousand years of worship?
A) It was accepted because of its length.
B) It was rejected because he lacked correct belief.
C) It was accepted because he never gave up.
D) It was less than the angels' worship.

Key Takeaway
Deeds without correct belief (tawhid) are like scattered dust, as seen in the example of Iblis and confirmed by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If I were to die tonight, would my deeds be accepted based on the state of my belief? What one step can I take this week to strengthen my tawhid?
?
The example of Iblis shows that even eighty thousand years of worship is worthless without correct belief. What does this teach me about my daily prayers and acts of worship? Am I relying on my deeds or on Allah's mercy and correct belief?

The Futility of Deeds Without Correct Belief
Sanusi warns that worship without correct tawhid is worthless, citing Iblis and Qur'anic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why deeds performed without correct belief in tawhid are worthless, as exemplified by Iblis and confirmed by the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Deeds without correct tawhid are scattered dust.

This lesson dives into a fundamental principle: that proper belief in Allah's oneness is the very foundation of all worship. Sanusi illustrates this with the shocking example of Iblis, who worshipped for millennia yet gained nothing, and reinforces it with powerful Qur'anic verses. Understanding this will help you see why the science of tawhid is the first obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning about corrupted belief
Begin by reading the passage carefully. Notice how Sanusi describes the state of one who worships outwardly while his heart is corrupt: the deeds become scattered dust.
2
Examine the example of Iblis
Contemplate the striking example of Iblis: he worshipped Allah for eighty thousand years without tiring, yet none of it benefited him because his belief was corrupt. This shows the sheer importance of correct belief over mere action.
Consider why Iblis's long worship did not save him.
3
Reflect on the Qur'anic verses and supplication
Read the two Quranic verses (Al-Furqan 23 and An-Nur 39) that Sanusi cites. They liken the deeds of disbelievers to scattered dust and a mirage. End with the supplication, which asks Allah for true knowledge and a good end.
Notice that both verses emphasize the ultimate worthlessness of deeds without faith.

Misery and eternity in painful punishment, and He does not expand his chest for good knowledge of Him, Exalted is He. And sometimes He, Exalted, merely impels the limbs to worship while the heart of its owner is concealing corruption in belief, so all those deeds become scattered dust, and its owner has from them nothing but mere fatigue, as He did with Iblis the accursed in the period of eighty thousand years during which he worshipped Allah without tiring, and Allah did not benefit him with any of it. And this is the state of one who does not care about knowing the first obligation upon him, which is the science of tawhid (علم التوحيد). Allah, Exalted, said: {And We will approach what they have done of deeds and make them scattered dust} [Al-Furqan: 23], and He, Mighty and Majestic, said: {And those who disbelieve, their deeds are like a mirage in a desert which the thirsty supposes is water until when he comes to it he finds it nothing and finds Allah with him and He pays him his account in full, and Allah is swift in account} [An-Nur: 39]. We ask Him, Glorified, for good knowledge of Him, and that He not deprive us of His great bounty, and that He bestow upon us a good end and forgiveness for all sins without trial in this world or the next.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a moral and doctrinal exhortation about the absolute necessity of correct belief (tawhid) for any deed to be accepted. The author begins by describing the consequence of lacking true knowledge of Allah: misery and eternal punishment. He explains that a person may perform outward acts of worship while his heart harbors corruption in belief; such deeds are like scattered dust—worthless, and the doer gains only fatigue. To illustrate this, he cites the example of Iblis (Satan), who worshiped Allah for eighty thousand years without ceasing, yet none of it benefited him because his belief was corrupt. This, he states, is the condition of anyone who neglects the first obligation: the science of tawhid (علم التوحيد). He then quotes two Quranic verses: Surah Al-Furqan 23, which says that the deeds of the disbelievers will be made like scattered dust, and Surah An-Nur 39, which compares their deeds to a mirage that a thirsty person thinks is water but finds nothing. Finally, the author concludes with a supplication asking Allah for good knowledge of Him, forgiveness, and a good end without trial.

The Fatwa Question on Utterance Without Knowledge
Sanusi reports a question to the fuqaha about utterance without knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context of a fatwa sought from the jurists of Bijaya regarding whether uttering the kalima without understanding suffices for faith.

Core Idea
Faith requires knowledge; mere utterance is questioned by the fuqaha.

This passage presents a real-world application of the theological discussion on faith and utterance. Sanusi mentions that the jurists of Bijaya and other imams were asked about a person who says 'la ilaha illa Allah' without understanding its meaning. This question tests the boundaries of what constitutes valid faith and shows how scholarly opinion was sought on practical cases.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic phrase for the fatwa question and its English translation. Notice the key terms: 'فقهاء بجاية' (jurists of Bijaya) and 'فتوى' (fatwa).
Bijaya is a historical city in North Africa (now Bejaia, Algeria).
2
Understand the context
This question arises from the earlier discussion on whether faith requires knowledge or just verbal confession. The fuqaha were consulted to give a ruling on a person who utters the kalima without knowing its meaning.
The answer is not provided here, but the question itself is significant.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this question matters: if utterance without knowledge is accepted as faith, then ignorance would be excused. If not, then knowledge is essential. This shows the practical stakes of theological definitions.
This connects to broader debates about takfir and salvation.

فتوى فقهاء بجاية في حقّ الناطق بكلمة التوحيدِ مِنْ غير دراية وقد سُئِلَ فقهاء بجَايَةَ وغيرُهم مِنَ الأئمة في أوائل هذا القرن أو قبله
Fatwa of the jurists of Bijaya regarding the one who utters the word of tawhid without knowledge. And the jurists of Bijaya and others among the imams were asked in the early part of this century or before it.

The question concerns the ruling regarding a person who utters the word of tawhid (la ilaha illa Allah) without knowledge or understanding. Unfortunately, the answer is not present in this text. The passage serves as a practical application of the previous discussion: the fuqaha were consulted about the issue Sanusi just raised—whether mere utterance suffices for faith. The incomplete nature of this text may be due to a page break or missing material.

The Shahada Requires Understanding, Not Just Utterance
Sanusi states that the Shahada encompasses all beliefs and that understanding is necessary for faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Shahada must be understood and believed in the heart, not merely spoken, and how it encompasses all Islamic beliefs.

Core Idea
The Shahada is the key to faith, but only if its meaning is known.

Sanusi now draws a crucial conclusion from his discussion of divine attributes. He emphasizes that the Shahada, though brief, summarizes all Islamic beliefs. But mere utterance is not enough—faith requires understanding. This passage establishes the linkage between knowledge, tawhid, and true faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal English translation. Notice how Sanusi first discusses two types of properties (shar'i and 'aqli) before applying them to the Shahada.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Focus on the Shahada's comprehensiveness
Identify the line where Sanusi states that the word of tawhid 'encompasses all the beliefs of faith in full.' This is a key claim about the Shahada's role.
Consider why this makes the Shahada the central declaration of Islam.
3
Understand the conclusion about faith
Sanusi ends with a strong warning: mere utterance without understanding is insufficient for true faith. Reflect on why understanding and inner knowledge are necessary.
This directly counters the misconception that lip service alone saves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معرفة سائر الخواص يتوقف على تحقيق مذهب أهل السنة ثم من الخواص ما هو شرعي كاستحقاق العبادة من الصلاة والزكاة والحج ونحو ذلك، ومنها ما هو عقلي كوجوب القدم والبقاء له تعالى في ذاته وصفاته ونحو ذلك. فقد بان لك بهذا أن فهم كلمة التوحيد ومعرفتها يتوقف على معرفة ما يليق بالإله الحق من الصفات ليعرف الموحد ما أثبت بكلمة التوحيد لمولانا جل وعز ونفاه عن جميع ما سواه. وظهر لك بهذا الذي ذكرناه أن كلمة التوحيد تتضمن على اختصارها جميع عقائد الإيمان على التمام، ولهذا جعلت في ظاهر الحكم الشرعي علما على الإيمان. ومن هنا تعرف أن مجرد النطق بهذه الكلمة من غير تحقق لمعناها، ولا معرفة في القلب لمدلولها لا يكفي في حصول حقيقة الإيمان.
Knowledge of the remaining properties depends on verifying the school of Ahl al-Sunna. Then among the properties are those that are legal (shar'i), like the obligation of worship from prayer, zakat, hajj, and so on; and among them are those that are rational ('aqli), like the necessity of pre-eternity and everlastingness for Him, Exalted, in His essence and attributes, and so on. So it has become clear to you by this that understanding the word of tawhid and knowing it depends on knowing what befits the True God of attributes, so that the muwahhid knows what he affirms by the word of tawhid for our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and what he negates from all other than Him. And it has become apparent to you by what we have mentioned that the word of tawhid, despite its conciseness, encompasses all the beliefs (aqa'id) of faith in full, and for this reason it was made in the apparent legal ruling a sign (alam) for faith. And from this you know that mere utterance of this word without verification of its meaning, and without knowledge in the heart of its import, is not sufficient for attaining the reality of faith.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a series of conclusions drawn by the author. He first establishes that understanding the remaining properties (presumably of God) depends on verifying the creed of Ahl al-Sunna. He then distinguishes between two types of properties: legal (shar'i) like worship obligations, and rational ('aqli) like God's pre-eternity and everlastingness. Applying this to the Shahada, he states that understanding the word of tawhid requires knowledge of the attributes that befit the True God, so that the person who affirms tawhid knows what he affirms of God and negates of others. He then emphasizes that the Shahada, despite its conciseness, encompasses all beliefs of faith completely, which is why it is treated in Islamic law as the mark of faith. Finally, he concludes that mere utterance of the words without understanding or internal knowledge is insufficient for attaining the reality of faith. The author's argument proceeds from the nature of the Shahada to its implications: it must be understood, not merely uttered.

Key Terms
كلمة التوحيد
عقائد الإيمان
حقيقة الإيمان
الخواص الشرعية
الخواص العقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that simply saying the Shahada out loud is enough to become a believer, regardless of understanding or inner conviction.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly says that mere utterance without verification of meaning and knowledge in the heart is not sufficient for attaining the reality of faith.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is required for the Shahada to constitute true faith?
A) Utterance of the words
B) Understanding of its meaning and knowing God's attributes
C) Performance of prayers and fasting
D) Being born among Muslims

Key Takeaway
The Shahada is the comprehensive statement of faith, but it must be understood and believed, not merely uttered.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Shahada in your prayers or daily life, do you consciously affirm God's unique attributes and negate any resemblance to creation, or has it become a routine utterance? Will you now pause to reflect on its meaning each time you say it?
?

?
Have you ever relied on the mere utterance of the Shahada as a guarantee of faith, while neglecting to deepen your understanding of its implications? What concrete step will you take today to ensure your faith goes beyond words into genuine knowledge?

Fatwa on Pronouncing Shahada Without Understanding
Sanusi reports a fatwa on the necessity of understanding the Shahada for faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why uttering the Shahada without understanding its meaning does not constitute faith, and how this case differs from belief through taqlid.

Core Idea
Understanding is essential; mere uttering of the Shahada without comprehension yields no share in Islam.

This lesson examines a famous fatwa from the jurists of Bijaya regarding a person who performs all Islamic rituals but without any understanding of the Shahada. Sanusi presents the question, the unanimous answer, and then clarifies that the real scholarly dispute is about belief through blind imitation, not about complete ignorance. This case sharpens our understanding of the relationship between external actions and internal conviction in defining true faith.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Read the description of the man who performs all Islamic actions but only as external forms without any understanding of the Shahada. Notice that he does not even know what he affirms or negates.
The scenario highlights the complete absence of comprehension.
2
Grasp the ruling
The jurists unanimously rule that such a person has no share in Islam. Reflect on the implication: external actions without understanding do not constitute faith.
3
Distinguish from taqlid
Sanusi then explains that the real controversy is about a person who does understand and is certain, but only through blind imitation (taqlid), not through proof. Compare the two cases.
This distinction is crucial for understanding different levels of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد سئل فقهاء بجاية وغيرهم من الأئمة في أوائل هذا القرن أو قبله عن رجل ينطق بكلمتي الشهادة، ويصلي ويصوم ويحج، يسير ويفعل كذا وكذا، لكن إنما يأتي بمجرد صور الأقوال والأعمال فقط على حسب ما يرى الناس يقولون ويعملون، حتى إنه ينطق بكلمتي الشهادة ولا يفهم لها معنى، ولا يدرك معنى الإله ولا معنى الرسول. وبالجملة: فلا يدري من كلمتي الشهادة ما أثبت ولا ما نفى، وربما توهم أن الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام نظير الإله، لما أنه رآه لازم الذكر معه في كلمتي الشهادة وفي كثير من المواضع؛ فهل ينتفع هذا الشخص بما صدر منه من صورة القول والفعل، ويصدق عليه حقيقة الإيمان فيما بينه وبين ربه أم لا؟ فأجابوا كلهم: بأن مثل هذا لا يضرب له في الإسلام بنصيب وإن صدر منه من صور أقوال الإيمان وأفعاله ما وقع. قلت: وهذا الذي أفتوا به في حق هذا الشخص ومن كان على حالته جلي في غاية الجلاء، لا يمكن أن يختلف فيه اثنان، وإنما نزاع العلماء واختلافهم فيمن عرف مدلول الشهادتين، وجزم بما تضمنته من عقائد التوحيد من غير تردد، إلا أن موجب جزمه بذلك التقليد، ومجرد النشأة بين قوم مؤمنين من غير أن يعرف برهاناً على ذلك أصلاً.
And the jurists of Bijaya and other imams were asked in the early part of this century or before about a man who pronounces the two testimonies (shahadatayn), and prays, fasts, performs Hajj, travels, and does such and such, but he only performs the mere forms of words and deeds according to what he sees people saying and doing, such that he pronounces the two testimonies but does not understand their meaning, nor does he grasp the meaning of 'ilah' (god) nor the meaning of 'rasul' (messenger). In short: he does not know from the two testimonies what he affirmed nor what he negated, and perhaps he imagines that the messenger, peace be upon him, is like the god, because he sees him constantly mentioned with Him in the two testimonies and in many places. So does this person benefit from what issued from him of the form of word and deed, and is the reality of faith (haqiqat al-iman) truly ascribed to him between him and his Lord, or not? They all answered: that such a person has no share in Islam, even if there issued from him forms of words and deeds of faith. I say: This fatwa regarding this person and whoever is in his state is extremely clear, no two can differ about it. Rather, the dispute and difference among scholars is concerning one who knows the import of the two testimonies, and is certain of the beliefs of tawhid they contain without hesitation, but the cause of his certainty is blind imitation (taqlid) and mere upbringing among believing people, without him knowing any proof for that at all.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents a fatwa and the author's analysis. The question describes a man who performs all Islamic rituals—prayer, fasting, Hajj, etc.—but only as external forms, imitating others without any understanding of the Shahada. He does not know what the Shahada affirms or negates, and might even consider the Prophet equal to God because they are mentioned together. The jurists unanimously reply that such a person has no share in Islam, regardless of his external actions. The author then comments that this ruling is absolutely clear and undisputed. He explains that the real scholarly controversy concerns a different case: a person who does understand the Shahada and is certain of its teachings, but his certainty comes from blind imitation (taqlid) and upbringing, without any rational proof. So the passage distinguishes between complete ignorance of the Shahada's meaning, which invalidates faith entirely, and belief through taqlid, which is a matter of dispute.

Key Terms
كلمتي الشهادة
حقيقة الإيمان
التقليد
فقهاء بجاية
الإله
الرسول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Performing all Islamic rituals without understanding the Shahada can still earn one the reality of faith.
Correction: The jurists unanimously state that such a person has no share in Islam, because true faith requires at least some understanding of what is being professed.

Checkpoint
What was the unanimous ruling of the jurists of Bijaya regarding the man who pronounces the Shahada without understanding its meaning?
A) He is a true believer
B) He has no share in Islam
C) He must repeat the Shahada with understanding
D) He is a hypocrite

Key Takeaway
Understanding the words of the Shahada is a necessary condition for true faith; mere imitation without comprehension does not make one a believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Shahada, do you actively engage your mind to affirm its meaning, or do your lips move while your heart remains distant? What one change can you make this week to ensure your declaration is not mere repetition?
?
If you were asked to explain the Shahada to someone who has never heard it, could you clearly state what it affirms and negates? If not, what will you do to gain that clarity, knowing that understanding is essential for your faith?
?
Have you ever assumed that your Islamic rituals—prayer, fasting, Hajj—alone are enough to guarantee your salvation, without checking whether your heart truly understands and believes the core testimony? How does this lesson challenge that assumption in your own life?

Ruling on Outward Acts Without Understanding
Sanusi presents a question and the scholars' fatwa on outward observance without understanding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true faith requires understanding and conviction in the meaning of the shahada, not just outward performance.

Core Idea
Faith is not mere imitation; it requires inner understanding.

Sanusi presents a hypothetical case of a person who performs all Islamic rituals but does not grasp their meaning. The scholars' unanimous ruling makes a crucial point: the reality of faith hinges on comprehension, not just action. Let's examine this case.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to familiarize yourself with its structure. Then read the literal translation.
2
Identify the key elements
Note the actions of the person (shahada, prayer, fasting, Hajj) and his lack of understanding.
He pronounces the shahada but does not understand its meaning.
3
Focus on the scholars' answer
The scholars unanimously say he has no share in Islam. Mark that conclusion.
4
Reflect on why understanding is essential
Consider why outward acts without inner conviction are insufficient for true faith.
This connects to the concept of iman in Ahl al-Sunna.
5
Connect to the broader theme
This case sets the stage for the debate on taqlid, which will be covered in the next lesson.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن رجلٍ ينطق بكلمتي الشهادة، ويصلي ويصوم ويحج، ويفعل كذا وكذا، لكن إنما يأتي بمجرد صور الأقوال والأعمال فقط على حسب ما يرى الناس يقولون ويعملون، حتى إنه ينطق بكلمتي الشهادة ولا يفهم لها معنى، ولا يدرك معنى الإله ولا معنى الرسول. وبالجملة: فلا يدري من كلمتي الشهادة ما أثبت ولا ما نفى، وربما توهم أن الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام نظير الإله، لما أن رآه لازم الذكر معه في كلمتي الشهادة وفي كثير من المواضع؛ فهل ينتفع هذا الشخص بما صدر منه من صورة القول والفعل، ويصدق عليه حقيقة الإيمان فيما بينه وبين ربه أم لا؟ فأجابوا كلهم: بأن مثل هذا لا يضرب له في الإسلام بنصيب وإن صدر منه من صور أقوال الإيمان وأفعاله ما وقع. عود لذم التقليد في الأصولِ قلت: وهذا الذي أفتوا به في حق هذا الشخص ومن كان على حالته... جلي في غاية الجلاء، لا يمكن أن يختلف فيه اثنان، وإنما نزاع العلماء واختلافهم فيمن عرف مدلول الشهادتين، وجزم بما تضمنته من عقائد التوحيد من غير تردد، إلا أن موجب جزمه بذلك التقليد، ومجرد النشأة بين قوم مؤمنين من غير أن يعرف برهانا على ذلك أصلا. والخلاف في صحة إيمان هذا هو الخلاف المعروف في صحة التقليد في العقائد، وقد قدمنا ما في ذلك في شرح مقدمة هذه العقيدة
Concerning a man who pronounces the two words of testimony (shahadatayn), and prays, fasts, performs Hajj, and does such and such, but he only performs the mere forms of words and deeds according to what he sees people say and do, such that he pronounces the two words of testimony without understanding their meaning, neither grasping the meaning of 'the god' (al-ilah) nor the meaning of 'the messenger' (al-rasul). In short: he does not know from the two words of testimony what he affirms nor what he denies, and perhaps he fancies that the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him) is similar to God (al-ilah), since he sees him always mentioned together with Him in the two words of testimony and in many places. So does this person benefit from what issues from him of the form of speech and action, and does the reality of faith (iman) apply to him between him and his Lord, or not? They all answered: that such a person has no share in Islam, even if what issues from him of the forms of the words and acts of faith occurs. [Return to condemning taqlid in fundamentals.] I say: This ruling which they gave concerning this person and whoever is in his condition... is perfectly clear, concerning which no two can differ. Rather, the scholars' disagreement and difference is concerning one who knows the import of the two testimonies, and is certain of what they contain of the doctrines of tawhid without hesitation, except that the cause of his certainty is taqlid (blind following) and mere upbringing among believing people, without knowing any proof for it at all. The dispute about the validity of the faith of this latter is the well-known dispute about the validity of taqlid in doctrines, and we have already presented what pertains to that in the commentary on the introduction to this creed.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is both a fatwa (ruling) and a clarification. It begins with a hypothetical question: a person performs all outward religious acts—uttering the shahada, praying, fasting, Hajj—but does so merely by imitation, without understanding the meaning of the words. He does not grasp who God (al-ilah) is or who the Prophet (al-rasul) is; indeed, he might mistakenly equate the Prophet with God because they are constantly mentioned together. The question is whether such a person is considered a true believer and whether his acts are accepted. The scholars unanimously answer that he has no share in Islam, meaning his faith is invalid. The author then comments (qultu) that this ruling is obvious and uncontested. The real scholarly dispute, he explains, is about a different case: a person who does understand the meaning of the shahada and is convinced of its contents, but whose conviction arises solely from taqlid (blind following) and upbringing, without any rational proof. That is the well-known debate on the validity of taqlid in matters of creed, which the author says he has already addressed in his commentary on the introduction to this creed.

إيمان

Correction: The scholars' ruling shows that understanding and conviction are necessary; mere imitation without comprehension does not make a person a true believer.

D) He is like a sincere Muslim.

The Real Debate: Taqlid in Doctrines
Sanusi distinguishes between the clear ruling on ignorance and the scholarly debate on taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly dispute about the validity of faith based on taqlid (blind following) as opposed to the clear case of complete ignorance.

Core Idea
The genuine disagreement lies in the case of belief without proof, not in complete ignorance.

After the clear fatwa, Sanusi directs us to the real point of contention among scholars: the person who understands the shahada and is convinced, but only through taqlid. This is where the famous debate on taqlid in `aqida begins. Let's explore his clarification.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's comment (qultu)
Read the passage from 'I say (qultu)' to the end. This is Sanusi's own clarification.
2
Identify the two cases
First, the case of the ignorant person (clear ruling). Second, the case of the person who knows but relies on taqlid (disputed).
3
Understand the condition of the debated person
This person knows the meaning of the shahada and is certain of the doctrines of tawhid, but his certainty comes from upbringing and imitation, not proof.
4
Relate to the earlier topic of taqlid
The author mentions that the debate about this person is the well-known dispute on taqlid in doctrines, which he covered in the commentary on the introduction.
5
Reflect on the importance of proof
Consider why scholars might require evidence for valid faith, and the role of proof in Islamic theology.

Two Types of Hypocrisy and the Danger of Taqlid
Sanusi distinguishes two types of hypocrisy and corrects a hadith interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between conscious and unconscious hypocrisy and how blind following (taqlid) can lead to the latter.

Core Idea
Some hypocrites don't even know they are hypocrites; taqlid blinds them.

In this passage, Sanusi begins by addressing a critical obstacle to knowing the truth: the dominance of blind following (taqlid). He then introduces a crucial distinction between two types of hypocrisy—one known to the person and one unknown. He also clarifies a hadith to prevent misinterpretation, emphasizing that outward piety can mask inner polytheism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of hypocrisy
Read the first sentence: 'Indeed hypocrisy is of two types: hypocrisy that its owner knows, and hypocrisy that its owner does not know'. Notice the second type: the person is unaware.
This distinction is unique and important.
2
Understand the role of taqlid
The passage begins by saying 'they do not know that, due to the dominance of blind following'. Taqlid is the cause of ignorance.
3
Examine the hadith clarification
Sanusi clarifies that the hadith does not refer to open idolaters but to those who outwardly practice Islam while secretly worshipping idols.
This shows that hypocrisy can be hidden even from oneself.

وهم لا يعرفونَ ذلك ؛ لغلبة التقليد ولهذا قيلَ : إِنَّ النفاق على ضربين : نفاق يعرفُهُ صاحبه ، ونفاق لا يعرفه صاحبه . وليس المراد في هذا الحديثِ بقولِهِ : « وَفِيهَا مُنَافِقُوهَا » عبدةَ الأصنام في منازلهم سراً معَ إظهار الإسلام للناس ، والصلاة وأعمال البرِّ ؛ فإنَّ أولئكَ يتَّبعون الطواغيت فيمَنِ اتَّبَعَها ؛ لأنَّهم كانوا يعبدونَها مِن دونِ اللهِ ، فتسيّرهم إلى جهنَّمَ ) . ثم قال بعد كلام : ( قالَ أهل الإشارة في قوله تعالى : ﴿ فَضُرِبَ بَيْنَهُم بِسُورٍ لَّهُ بَابُ بَاطِنُهُ فِيهِ الرَّحْمَةُ وَظَهِرُهُ مِن قِبَلِهِ الْعَذَابُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٣] : مثال ذلك البابِ : قولُ : « لا إله إلا الله» كانَتْ في ألسنتهم كما كان المؤمنون يقولونَها ، وكانَ الإيمان والمعرفة والعلم بها في قلوبِ المؤمنين عن يقين وبرهان ، لا عن تقليد وتخمين وحسبان ، وهذا معنى قوله تعالى : ﴿ بَاطِنُهُ فِيهِ الرَّحْمَةُ وَظَهِرُهُ مِن قِبَلِهِ الْعَذَابُ ﴾ أي : ظاهرُ القول بلا معرفة إلا مجرَّدَ التقليدِ ، مِن قِبَلِهِ الْعَذَابُ ﴾ أي : مِنْ قِبَلِ ذلكَ الظاهرِ الذي هو التقليد يجيء العذابُ ، فأخذوا « لا إله إلا الله » مِنَ الناسِ مِنْ خارج ، وأخذ العارفونَ « لا إله إلا الله ، محمدٌ رسولُ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مِنْ بواطن قلوبهم ومعارفهم ، والله أعلم بسر غيبه " ولذلك جاءَ في الآية : يُنَادُونَهُمْ أَلَمْ تَكُن مَّعَكُمْ ) أي : كنا نقول الشهادتين كما كنتُم تقولونَ ، ونصلّي كما كنتُم تصلُّون ، ونحج ونجاهد ونصومُ كما كنتُم تفعلونَ ، وفي آخر الآية : ﴿ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغُرُورُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤] وهو الشيطانُ ولذلك قال أهل العلم : إذا هم أحدهم بأن ينظر أو يستدل . . صاح به شيطانهُ مِنَ الجِنِّ أو الإنس : أتريدُ أنْ تُشكك في دينك وأنت صحيحُ العَقدِ ثابتُ الإيمانِ ؟! حتى إذا جاءَهُ الموتُ شَكَكَهُ فتشكَّكَ فقالَ في القبرِ : سمعتُ الناس يقولون شيئاً فقلتُهُ ثم قال تعالى : ﴿ فَالْيَوْمَ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنكُمْ فِدْيَةٌ وَلَا مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ﴾ [الحديد : ١٥] ، ففرَّقَ بينهم وبينَ مَنْ كانَ يجاهرُ بالكفر والعياذُ باللهِ تعالى مِنَ الشكّ والشركِ والنفاقِ ( انتهى
And they do not know that, due to the dominance of blind following. For this reason it was said: Indeed hypocrisy is of two types: hypocrisy that its owner knows, and hypocrisy that its owner does not know. And what is intended in this hadith by his statement: 'And among them are its hypocrites' is not the idolaters who secretly worship idols in their homes while outwardly showing Islam, prayer, and good deeds; for those follow the false deities among those who followed them, because they used to worship them besides Allah, so they will be driven to Hell. Then he said after some speech: The people of spiritual insight said regarding the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then a wall will be placed between them, with a gate, the inner side of it contains mercy, and the outer side of it is from before it is punishment' [al-Hadid:13]: An example of that gate is the statement: 'There is no god but Allah'—it was on their tongues as the believers used to say it, but faith, knowledge, and understanding of it were in the hearts of the believers with certainty and proof, not from blind following, conjecture, and estimation. This is the meaning of His saying: 'The inner side of it contains mercy, and the outer side of it is from before it is punishment'—that is, the outward saying without knowledge except mere blind following, 'from before it is punishment'—that is, from that outward aspect which is blind following comes the punishment. So they took 'There is no god but Allah' from people from the outside, and the knowers took 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace)' from the inward depths of their hearts and their knowledge. And Allah knows best the secret of His unseen. And therefore it came in the verse: 'They will call out to them: Were we not with you?'—that is, we used to say the two testimonies as you used to say, and pray as you used to pray, and perform pilgrimage, jihad, and fasting as you used to do. And at the end of the verse: 'And the Deceiver deceived you about Allah' [al-Hadid:14]—and he is Satan. And therefore the people of knowledge said: When one of them intends to look or to infer... his devil from among the jinn or humans shouts at him: Do you want to cast doubt in your religion while you are sound in creed and firm in faith?! Until when death comes to him, it makes him doubt, and he becomes doubtful. So he says in the grave: I heard the people saying something, so I said it. Then Allah Most High says: 'So today no ransom will be taken from you nor from those who disbelieved' [al-Hadid:15], so He distinguished between them and those who were blatant in disbelief (and we seek refuge with Allah Most High from doubt, polytheism, and hypocrisy). (End)
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on hypocrisy (nifaq) and blind following (taqlid), beginning with the statement that hypocrisy is of two types: one the person himself recognizes, and another he does not. The author clarifies that the hadith reference to 'its hypocrites' does not refer to open idolaters, but to those who outwardly practice Islam while inwardly worshipping idols. He then cites an interpretation by the 'people of spiritual insight' (ahl al-ishara) of the Quranic verse about a wall with a gate (al-Hadid:13). They take the gate as the statement 'La ilaha illallah'. The hypocrites utter it on their tongues, but the believers utter it from certainty and proof. The inner side of the gate (the heart) contains mercy for the believers, while the outer side (the mere utterance without knowledge) brings punishment. This is because the hypocrites took the word from people externally, while the true knowers took it from the depths of their hearts. The author then connects this to the later verse where the hypocrites ask 'Were we not with you?'—meaning they performed the same outward acts—but they were deceived by Satan, who prevents them from seeking proof. When they try to investigate, their devil scares them, so they remain in taqlid until death when doubt overcomes them, and they say in the grave 'I heard people saying something so I said it'. Finally, the author distinguishes them from open disbelievers, seeking refuge from doubt, polytheism, and hypocrisy.

Key Terms
نفاق
تقليد
نفاق يعرفه
نفاق لا يعرفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All hypocrites know they are hypocrites.
Correction: The passage teaches that there is a type of hypocrisy that the person themselves does not recognize, often due to blind following.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main cause of people not knowing the truth about hypocrisy?
A) Lack of intelligence
B) Dominance of blind following (taqlid)
C) Weak faith
D) Lack of religious practice

Key Takeaway
True hypocrisy can be hidden from the person himself; taqlid is the root cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you assume that because you pray and do good deeds, your faith is secure? How do you know you are not secretly following false ideas or desires that you have never examined?
?
What beliefs or practices have you inherited from your family or community without questioning their source? Could they be a form of taqlid hiding a deeper hypocrisy?
?
If Allah were to ask you today for the basis of your Islam, would you point to your upbringing or to a conscious, examined faith? What will you do this week to uncover any hidden hypocrisy within you?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
7 min
The Quranic Metaphor: Taqlid vs. Certainty in Faith
Sanusi interprets Quranic verse to contrast taqlid with certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verse about the wall with a gate illustrates the difference between faith based on certainty and faith based on blind following.

Core Idea
Mere utterance of shahada without inner certainty brings punishment; only heart-based certainty brings mercy.

In this profound spiritual interpretation, Sanusi draws on the verse from Surat al-Hadid to illustrate the fate of those who merely repeat the testimony of faith without understanding. He explains how Satan prevents them from seeking proof, leading them to die in doubt. This passage is a warning against taqlid and a call for certainty.

Guided Path
1
Understand the metaphor of the gate
The 'people of insight' interpret the gate as the statement 'La ilaha illallah'. The inner side (heart) contains mercy for believers, and the outer side (tongue) leads to punishment for hypocrites.
The key is whether the shahada is in the heart with certainty or just on the tongue.
2
Recognize the danger of taqlid
The hypocrites took the shahada from people externally, while the believers had it from within through certainty and proof.
3
See the role of Satan
When the hypocrite intends to seek evidence, Satan whispers: 'Do you want to doubt your religion?', so they refrain.
This shows how taqlid is reinforced by devilish whispers.
4
Reflect on the deathbed scene
At death, doubt overcomes them, and they say in the grave: 'I heard people saying something, so I said it.' Then no ransom is accepted.
This is a tragic end for those who followed without knowledge.

If you were to die tonight, would your faith be based on proof or on following others? What is one concrete step you can take today to turn your faith into certainty?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

Answering the Fear of Taqlid: Self-Examination and Certainty
Sanusi answers an objection about fear from taqlid and gives criteria to distinguish it from knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how to distinguish between blind following (taqlid) and true knowledge by examining your own conscience against sound definitions.

Core Idea
Self-examination and understanding definitions turn fear about faith into clarity.

Sanusi addresses a real concern: the condemnation of taqlid can cause anxiety about the validity of one's own beliefs. But he does not leave the reader in doubt. Instead, he provides a practical method—learn the reality of taqlid and knowledge, then honestly examine your inner conviction. This lesson shows how to apply that method.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening objection carefully: The reader fears that Sanusi's repeated condemnation of taqlid makes him doubt his own faith and that of most common Muslims. Notice the emotional weight—'great fear and bad suspicion.'
The objection is real and common among students of kalam.
2
Grasp the author's answer
Sanusi replies that a person knows himself best. No one else can judge his inner state. So the solution is internal, not external. Identify the key phrase: 'he knows himself best.'
This shifts responsibility from scholars to the individual.
3
Learn the two definitions
Sanusi says one must ask about the reality of taqlid and the reality of knowledge (ma'rifa). These are the two categories. Understanding their true meanings is essential before self-examination.
Taqlid is blind acceptance without evidence; ma'rifa is certain knowledge based on proof.
4
Apply self-examination using conscience
After learning the definitions, compare them with what is in your conscience (damir). Your inner conviction will reveal which category your faith falls into. This is an honest assessment, not a theoretical exercise.
Conscience here refers to the inner sense of certainty or doubt.
5
Seek sound doctrines
Finally, Sanusi adds: actively seek correct doctrines (al-aqa'id al-sahiha). This implies that if you find your faith lacking, you should study sound creed. The path out of fear involves both self-knowledge and pursuit of truth.
This makes the method actionable, not merely introspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : هذا الذي تقرِّرُهُ المُرَّةَ بعد المرَّةِ في ذم التقليد وتهويل أمرِه . . أوجب لنا خوفاً عظيماً ، وسوء ظن بعقائدِنا وبعقائدِ أكثر عوام المسلمينَ ، فما المُخلَّصُ مِنْ ذلكَ ؟ قلتُ : أما الإنسانُ باعتبار نفسِهِ : فهو أعرفُ بها ، ولا يُسأل عنها غيرُه ، فإذا أرادَ أنْ يعرفَ قَدْرَ نفسِهِ في العقائدِ فليسأل عن حقيقة التقليد ، وعن حقيقة المعرفةِ ؛ حتى يُميّز إحداهما عن الأخرى تمييزاً صحيحاً ، وليعرض ذلك على ما في ضميره ؛ فإنَّه سيعرفُ ما هو الحاصلُ لهُ مِنَ الحقيقتين ، وليبحث عن العقائدِ الصحيحة أيضاً
If you say: This that you have repeated time and again in condemnation of blind following and making its matter seem grave has caused us great fear and bad suspicion of our own creeds and the creeds of most common Muslims, so what is the way out from that? I say: As for a person with regard to himself, he knows himself best, and no one else is asked about him. So if he wants to know his own standing in matters of creed, let him ask about the reality of blind follow and about the reality of knowledge, so that he may distinguish one from the other correctly, and let him compare that with what is in his conscience; for he will know which of the two realities is present in him, and let him also seek sound creeds.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (فإن قلت...قلت) structure. The objector says that the author's repeated condemnation of taqlid (blind following) and his strong warnings have caused fear and suspicion about the validity of their own faith and that of most common Muslims. The author's answer: A person knows himself best and others are not responsible for his inner state. To assess his own standing, he must first learn the true definitions of taqlid and knowledge (ma'rifa). Then he should honestly examine his own conscience: does his faith rest on mere acceptance from others, or on personal certainty and evidence? He will then know which of the two he possesses. Furthermore, he should actively seek correct doctrines (i.e., study sound creed). Thus, the path out of fear is self-examination guided by proper understanding of the concepts.

Key Terms
تقليد
معرفة
عقائد
ضمير
حقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think it is impossible to know whether one is in taqlid or has true knowledge.
Correction: The author insists that one can discern it by learning the definitions of taqlid and knowledge and then honestly examining his own conscience.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, how can a person know whether he is in taqlid or has true knowledge?
A) By asking a scholar
B) By learning the reality of taqlid and knowledge and examining his conscience
C) By performing many good deeds
D) By waiting for a divine sign

Key Takeaway
Anyone can distinguish between genuine faith and imitation by learning the definitions of taqlid and knowledge and honestly examining their own inner conviction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to honestly compare your own faith to the definition of taqlid given here, would you be able to say with certainty that you are not a blind follower? What specific evidence in your heart would you point to?
?
Sanusi says 'a person with regard to himself knows himself best, and no one else is asked about him.' Have you ever been too afraid to look inside and ask yourself whether your faith is truly yours or just inherited? What might it cost you to continue avoiding that self-examination?
?
You now know that the key is to learn the definitions and examine yourself. After reading this lesson, what concrete step will you take tonight to move from fear to certainty — will you write down the definitions, or will you sit in solitude to question your conscience? Be specific.

The Deception of Shaytan and the Trial of the Grave
A quoted passage describing shaytan's deception and the grave trial for those who follow taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how shaytan deceives those who rely on taqlid, causing doubt at death and failure in the grave trial.

Core Idea
Blind following makes you an easy target for shaytan's final whisper.

This passage from the scholars warns of a subtle danger: merely mimicking others' faith without personal conviction. Shaytan exploits this weakness, preventing investigation in life and then shaking the person at death, leading to doubt in the grave. The lesson contrasts such people with those who openly disbelieve, showing that taqlid is not a safe path.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the narrative flow before interpreting.
The passage begins with 'الشهادتين' which is a continuation from a previous sentence.
2
Identify the deception strategy
Notice that shaytan shouts at the person who intends to investigate his faith, warning that he will cast doubt on his sound belief. This is the first stage of deception.
3
Recognize the consequence at death
When death comes, shaytan shakes the person, causing doubt. This doubt is the fruit of taqlid and lack of certain knowledge.
4
Understand the grave confession
In the grave, the person admits: 'I heard people saying something, so I said it.' This shows that taqlid provides no refuge in the trial.
5
Reflect on the verse and distinction
Allah quotes the verse stating no ransom will be accepted, and distinguishes these people from open disbelievers. Consider the severity of this position.

Then Allah Almighty said: {So today no ransom shall be taken from you nor from those who disbelieved} [al-Hadid:15], and He distinguished between them and those who openly disbelieved — and we seek refuge in Allah Almighty from doubt, polytheism, and hypocrisy. Commentary
This passage is a quotation from the people of knowledge, likely concluding a discussion on the danger of taqlid. It begins by recounting a scenario where someone intends to investigate his religion, but his shaytan dissuades him, warning that he will cast doubt on his sound faith. As a result, the person remains in taqlid and does not seek certain knowledge. When death comes, the shaytan shakes him, causing doubt, and in the grave he confesses that he merely followed what others said. Then the verse from Surat al-Hadid is cited, stating that on that day no ransom will be accepted from them, and Allah distinguishes them from those who openly disbelieved. The passage ends with a plea for refuge from doubt, polytheism, and hypocrisy. The core warning is that taqlid leaves one vulnerable to shaytan's deception both in this life and in the grave.

Ruling: No Bad Suspicion of Any Muslim's Faith
Sanusi declares the ruling and explains its implications for common Muslims and scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why we must not have bad suspicion of any Muslim's faith, and what suffices for a common Muslim to be considered a knower.

Core Idea
Understanding a general proof makes a Muslim a knower, regardless of ability to debate.

This lesson presents a crucial ruling in Islamic creed: we must not assume bad faith about any Muslim, even if we cannot see their hearts. The author explains that true knowledge is in the heart, and a simple understanding of a general proof is enough to exit blind following. This guards against unjust suspicion and clarifies the role of scholars in defending the faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the ruling and its reason
Read the first part of the passage where the author states the ruling and gives the reason: knowledge is in the heart.
Notice that the ruling is emphatic: 'we must not have bad suspicion'.
2
Identify what suffices and what is not required
The passage lists three things not required for a common Muslim to exit taqlid. Find them and note that only understanding a general proof (dalil jumli) is sufficient.
These are key to understanding the leniency of the Sharia.
3
Understand the definition of a 'knower'
See how the author defines a knower (arif): someone who understands the truth through the proof, even if they cannot express it or refute doubts.
This expands the category of scholars.
4
Recognize the communal obligation
Learn that the duty to refute doubts is a communal obligation (fard kifaya) for scholars, not for every Muslim.
This protects common Muslims from being blamed for not debating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ لا يجوز سوء الظنِّ بإيمانِ أحدٍ مِنَ المسلمينَ ] ثم مع هذا فليس لنا أنْ نُسِيءَ الظَّنَّ بإيمانِ أحدٍ مِنَ المسلمينَ ، عاميّاً كان أو غيره ؛ إذ المعرفة محلها القلبُ ، والتقليد يكفي في الخروج منه الدليلُ الجُمْلي ، ولا يُشترط القدرة على ترتيبه على الوجهِ الذي يُرتبه العلماء ، ولا دفعِ الشُّبَهِ الواردة عليه ، ولا القدرة على التعبير عنه ، بل إذا فهمَهُ فَهْماً عرف بهِ الحق ، وخرج به عن التقليد . فهو عارفٌ وإِنْ لم يقدر أن يُعبّرَ عمَّا في ضميرِهِ مِنْ ذلكَ ، ولا قَدَرَ أَنْ يراً على مبتدع شبهةً يوردها على الحقِّ ؛ لأنَّ ذلكَ وظيفةُ العلماء الراسخين في العلم ، وهو فرضُ كفايةٍ ، مَنْ قامَ بِهِ مِنَ العلماء في كلِّ قُطْرِ أَجزاً عن غيرِهِ مِنْ ذلكَ القُطْرِ
[It is not permissible to have bad suspicion of the faith of any Muslim.] Then despite this, we must not have bad suspicion of the faith of any Muslim, whether a commoner or otherwise, because knowledge has its place in the heart, and in exiting from taqlid it is sufficient to have the general proof, and it is not required to be able to arrange it in the manner that scholars arrange it, nor to refute the doubts that come against it, nor to be able to express it. Rather, if he understands it in a way that he knows the truth through it, he exits from taqlid. So he is a knower even if he cannot express what is in his conscience of that, nor can he refute a doubt that an innovator brings against the truth, because that is the function of the deeply rooted scholars in knowledge, and it is a communal obligation. Whoever among the scholars in every region performs it suffices for others in that region.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a ruling. It establishes a clear principle: we must not assume the worst about any Muslim's faith. The reason is that true knowledge (ma'rifa) is in the heart, and a person can exit taqlid by simply understanding a general proof (dalil jumli). It is not necessary to be able to articulate it like a scholar, nor to defend it against doubts, nor to express it verbally. If a person understands the proof well enough to know the truth through it, he is considered a knower (arif) and is no longer a mere imitator. The ability to debate with innovators is a specialized function of the scholars, which is a communal obligation (fard kifaya); if some scholars in a region fulfill it, others are absolved. This guards against suspecting common Muslims of being ignorant or following taqlid invalidly. They may have sufficient understanding even if they cannot express it.

تقليد
دليل جُملي
عارف
فرض كفاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A common Muslim who cannot argue against doubts is still in taqlid and not a true believer.
Correction: The passage clarifies that understanding a general proof suffices for knowledge (ma'rifa) and exiting taqlid, even without the ability to argue.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
We must not judge a Muslim's faith based on outward ability to debate; understanding a general proof suffices for true knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Which of your daily practices—prayer, study, conversation—reveals a heart that knows versus a mind that merely performs? Ask yourself tonight before you sleep: am I a knower, or just a good imitator?
?
Sanusi says refuting doubts is for scholars, not every Muslim. Are you burdened by the pressure to defend Islam against every criticism, and how does this teaching release you from that? At the same time, are you using this as an excuse to avoid learning the general proof? Do Not Think Ill of Any Muslim's Faith
Sanusi argues we must not assume taqlid due to inability to articulate proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi rules that it is impermissible to assume a Muslim's faith is defective simply because they cannot articulate proofs or refute doubts.

Core Idea
Knowledge of faith is in the heart, not the tongue.

Sanusi addresses a practical and sensitive issue: how do we judge the faith of fellow Muslims, especially those who cannot argue theology? He sets a clear rule: we must not think ill of anyone's faith, regardless of whether they are a scholar or a layperson. The key insight is that genuine knowledge (ma'rifa) resides in the heart, and a simple but sincere understanding of the proof suffices, even if one cannot express it beautifully or defend it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general principle
Read the first part about our ignorance of others' inner selves and the exception for prophetic testimony.
Sanusi reminds us that only Allah and His Messenger know what is truly in someone's heart.
2
Identify the ruling and its reason
Find the direct prohibition against thinking ill of any Muslim's faith, and note the reason given: knowledge is in the heart, and taqlid is sufficient with the comprehensive proof.
The comprehensive proof (dalīl jumlī) is a simple, holistic understanding of the truth.
3
Examine what is NOT required
List the three things that are not required for true faith: arranging proofs like scholars, refuting doubts, and being able to articulate the proofs. Understanding in the heart is enough.
This is a crucial point for avoiding harsh judgments.
4
Learn the collective obligation (farḍ kifāya)
Understand that the duty to argue and refute doubts falls on the scholars as a collective obligation, not on every individual.
This excuses the common person from being a theologian.
5
Apply the principle: do not assume taqlid
Read the conclusion: since articulate speech is not a condition, we cannot assume someone is a mere muqallid just because they cannot speak well. The only exception is if their words clearly indicate corrupt belief.
Even many scholars cannot express their deep knowledge eloquently.

[ لا يجوز سوء الظنِّ بإيمانِ أحدٍ مِنَ المسلمينَ ] ثم مع هذا فليس لنا أنْ نُسِيءَ الظَّنَّ بإيمانِ أحدٍ مِنَ المسلمينَ ، عاميّاً كان أو غيره ؛ إذ المعرفة محلها القلبُ ، والتقليد يكفي في الخروج منه الدليلُ الجُمْلي ، ولا يُشترط القدرة على ترتيبه على الوجهِ الذي يُرتبه العلماء ، ولا دفعِ الشُّبَهِ الواردة عليه ، ولا القدرة على التعبير عنه ، بل إذا فهمَهُ فَهْماً عرف بهِ الحق ، وخرج به عن التقليد . فهو عارفٌ وإِنْ لم يقدر أن يُعبّرَ عمَّا في ضميرِهِ مِنْ ذلكَ ، ولا قَدَرَ أَنْ يراً على مبتدع شبهةً يوردها على الحقِّ ؛ لأنَّ ذلكَ وظيفةُ العلماء الراسخين في العلم ، وهو فرضُ كفايةٍ ، مَنْ قامَ بِهِ مِنَ العلماء في كلِّ قُطْرِ أَجزاً عن غيرِهِ مِنْ ذلكَ القُطْرِ . وإذا عرفت أنَّ القدرة على تقديرِ الدليل والتعبير عنه ليس بشرط في المعرفة والخروج عن التقليد، بل فهمه في القلب هو المشترط .. لم يكن لنا أنْ نُسِيءَ الظَّنَّ بعامي أو غيره ، ولا أنْ نجزم في حقه بالتقليد بمُجرَّدِ عجز لسانِهِ عن تقرير أدلَّةِ العقائدِ ؛ لاحتمالِ أنْ يكونَ عارفاً بعقائدِ الإيمان وبأدلَّتِها ، لكن على وجه يعسر عليه التعبير عنها وكثيرٌ مِنَ العلماءِ يَعجزون عن التعبير عما في ضمائرهم مِنَ العلومِ المحققة ، فكيف بالعامَّةِ ؟! اللهم إلا أنْ يظهر على لسانِ امري ما يدلُّ عمَّا كَمَنَ في ضميرِهِ مِنَ العَقْدِ الفاسد ، فالواجب حينَئِذٍ أَنْ يُتلطَّفَ في تعليمِهِ ومعافاة دائِهِ بما أمكن ، والله المستعان
To know whether he was correct in his beliefs or not? In summary: So let him know the truth, he will know its people, and perplexity will leave him. And as for the human being considered from other's perspective: his lot is ignorance of the state of his conscience, and lack of certainty about anything concerning him according to what is in reality, unless the Lawgiver (peace and blessings be upon him) testifies about someone with something, then let him be certain about that in reality; for Allah Almighty and His Messenger know best. [It is not permissible to think ill of the faith of any of the Muslims] Then besides this, it is not for us to think ill of the faith of any of the Muslims, whether layperson or otherwise; for knowledge resides in the heart, and taqlid is sufficient for exiting (it) with the comprehensive proof (al-dalīl al-jumlī), and ability to arrange it in the manner scholars arrange it is not required, nor refuting doubts that arise against it, nor ability to express it, rather if he understands it with an understanding by which he knows the truth and exits from taqlid, then he is a knower (ʿārif) even if he cannot express what is in his heart of that, nor can he refute against an innovator a doubt he brings against the truth; because that is the function of the deeply rooted scholars (al-ʿulamāʾ al-rāsikhīn fī al-ʿilm), and it is a collective obligation (farḍ kifāya); whoever of the scholars in every region undertakes it suffices for others of that region. And if you know that ability to formulate the proof and express it is not a condition for knowledge and exiting taqlid, but rather understanding it in the heart is the prerequisite, then it is not for us to think ill of a layperson or other, nor to be certain about him being a muqallid merely because of his tongue's inability to articulate the proofs of the beliefs; due to the probability that he is knowledgeable in the beliefs of faith and their proofs, but in a way that it is difficult for him to express them. And many of the scholars cannot express the verified sciences in their hearts, so how about the common people?! Unless something appears on the tongue of a person indicating what lay hidden in his heart of corrupt belief (al-ʿaqd al-fāsid), then it is obligatory to be gentle in teaching him and treating his disease as much as possible. And Allah is the one whose help is sought.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is an argument about how we should judge the faith of others, especially common people. It begins by stating that we cannot know another's inner state unless the Lawgiver (the Prophet) testifies about it. Then it gives the ruling: it is not permissible to think ill of any Muslim's faith, whether layperson or scholar. The reason is that true knowledge resides in the heart, and taqlid (imitation) is sufficient for salvation if one has a comprehensive understanding (al-dalīl al-jumlī). The author lists things that are not required: the ability to arrange proofs like scholars, to refute doubts, or to articulate the proofs. If a person understands the proofs in his heart and comes to know the truth, he is a 'ārif (knower) even if he cannot express it or refute doubts. That task is the duty of deeply rooted scholars and is a collective obligation (farḍ kifāya). The author then concludes: since understanding in the heart is what matters, we cannot assume someone is merely a muqallid just because he cannot speak well. Many scholars themselves cannot articulate their verified knowledge, so common people are even more excused. The only exception is if someone's words clearly indicate inner corrupt belief; then gentle teaching and treatment is required.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that a person who cannot argue or refute doubts is not a true believer or is merely a blind follower (muqallid) without genuine faith.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that genuine knowledge (ma'rifa) can exist in the heart even if one lacks eloquence or debating skills. Understanding the truth with the comprehensive proof is sufficient to exit taqlid and be considered a knower ('ārif).

Key Takeaway
We must not judge a person's faith by their ability to articulate or defend it; what matters is the understanding in their heart.

Eloquence in Proofs Does Not Guarantee True Knowledge
Sanusi demonstrates the disconnect between articulate proof and genuine faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that eloquent presentation of proofs and refutation of doubts do not necessarily indicate true faith or knowledge, and that deep understanding can exist in unexpected people.

Core Idea
Articulate proof does not equal true knowledge.

This passage from Sanusi challenges a common assumption: that someone who speaks eloquently about theological proofs must possess genuine faith. Sanusi warns that the opposite can be true, and offers a striking historical example from earlier Islamic communities where even common people had profound understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to grasp the author's argument without interpretation.
Notice the contrast between the articulate person and the true knower.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that speaking with proofs and eloquent articulation does not necessarily accompany knowledge. Identify this central warning.
Sanusi uses 'لا يلازم' (does not necessarily accompany).
3
Examine the counterexample
Sanusi gives a specific scenario: someone may speak precisely and refute doubts while being ignorant or even doubtful, while a knowledgeable person may be unable to do so. Reflect on this inversion.
This challenges the common equation of eloquence with understanding.
4
Reflect on the historical example
Sanusi refers to past common people who had profound verification of knowledge, surpassing skilled scholars of his time. Consider what this says about the relationship between social status and true knowledge.
He mentions Ibn 'Arabi and others witnessing such phenomena.
5
Formulate the key takeaway
After studying the passage, summarize the lesson: eloquence is not a reliable indicator of genuine faith or knowledge. True understanding may be hidden.
This guards against judging others based on verbal skill alone.
